Overview of Education in Hangzhou 83

▲Recent Situation (Lu Dianyang)

(1) Education Funding

The 18th year budget for education expenditures in Hangzhou was projected to be 275,054 yuan for regular expenses and over 14,700 yuan for temporary expenses, totaling 290,000 yuan. This represents approximately 27% of the city's total revenue of over 1.11 million yuan. The 19th year budget will aim for 30% of total revenue. Hangzhou's financial policy adopts a unified collection and expenditure system for education funding. Funds are not specifically designated, but educational institutions receive monthly budget allocations without delays.

The 18th year funding for Hangzhou Municipal Junior High School was 20,815 yuan, approximately 7% of the total education budget. Primary school funding was 222,847.40 yuan, approximately 81% of the total education budget. This includes subsidies for all private primary schools and bonuses for private primary school teachers. The social education budget was only 10,039 yuan, approximately 4% of the total. However, actual spending, including transfers from reserve funds, reached about 7%. Educational administration expenses were 5,040 yuan, approximately less than 0.2% of the total. Teacher training institutes and other items accounted for about 6% of the total.

(2) School Education

(1) There is one municipal junior high school, which opened in the 17th year with separate divisions for boys and girls. Currently, there are 230 students in six grades.

(2) There are 67 municipal primary schools, including 18 complete primary schools and 49 junior primary schools, with a total of 247 classes and 10,880 students.

(3) There are 92 private primary schools, with 46 receiving subsidies, a total of 227 classes, and 10,728 students.

Li Shizeng

(4) The average annual government expenditure per junior high school student is 90.5 yuan. The average government expenditure per municipal primary school student is 19.2 yuan.

(5) The standard monthly salary for a municipal primary school head teacher is 34 yuan. There are currently 373 teachers, with an average monthly salary of 32.87 yuan. There are 445 private primary school teachers, with an average monthly salary of 19.41 yuan.

(6) There is one municipal teacher training institute, which admits unqualified primary school teachers.

Currently, there are 60 people, with an annual expenditure of 800 yuan, averaging 13.33 yuan per person per year.

(3) Social Education

(1) Adult Continuing Education

(A) There are currently nine evening schools for the common people, with twelve classes and 693 students. Each class receives 17 yuan per month, totaling 4 months, with the government covering an average of 1.2 yuan per student.

(B) There are currently three worker's supplementary schools: the Municipal Government Public Works Bureau Worker's Night School, the Sanyou Industrial Worker's Supplementary School, and the Rickshaw Pullers' Union Supplementary School. Funding is provided by each respective organization, with guidance and evaluation from the Municipal Government.

(C) Government Employee Literacy Classes: The Municipal Government and its affiliated agencies and organizations compel service workers to become literate. The first phase of independently or jointly organized literacy classes is limited to one month. It has already been completed, with an estimated increase of approximately 300 literate individuals.

(D) Student Literacy Teaching in Municipal Schools: Outstanding students in the sixth grade and above in senior primary schools each find one or two illiterate individuals to teach literacy for a period of one month. It is currently in the trial period, with an estimated increase of approximately 250 literate individuals. It will be gradually implemented in the future.

(2) Public Education Institutions

(A) Municipal Popular Library: One

(B) Municipal Children's Library: One

(C) Municipal Educational Book Depository: One

(D) Municipal Mobile Popular Library: Three

(E) Subsidized Private Zhejiang Circulation Library: One

(F) Municipal Natural Science Laboratory: One

(G) Municipal Botanical Garden: One

(H) Municipal Simple Sports Field: One

(I) Municipal Children's Playground: One

(J) Municipal Popular Lecture Hall: Six

(K) Municipal Improved Tea Garden: Two

(L) Literacy Centers: Sixty-seven (attached to each municipal primary school)

Implementation of Educational Plans and Local Educational Administration by Xia Chengfeng 84

During the ten-day session of this National Education Conference, the educational plans successfully developed by dozens of experts over several months will undoubtedly be revised to perfection. The value of these plans will only become evident after implementation begins. However, the difficulties encountered during implementation may not be entirely due to flaws in the plans themselves. During the discussions on the merits and demerits of the plans, it is also natural to open up one or several more crucial paths for their implementation. Otherwise, the various educational conferences held in our country over the past one or two decades, no matter how lively, and the so-called plans, no matter how numerous, have only resulted in the joy and encouragement on the conference floor and the flowery language in the conference reports. The resolutions are passed on to the desks of education directors and bureau chiefs. The important ones cannot be started, the secondary ones are lightly filed away, and those that do not align with personal tastes are not even worth a smile.

Experience tells us that such phenomena do indeed exist. The mission of this conference is at least related to the success or failure of education in the next two or three decades. We must have more precise discussions on the critical junctures in the implementation process of the plans in order to avoid repeating past mistakes. The so-called precondition to preconditions in the process is naturally the broad financing of education. However, even if educational funding experiences rapid development in one or two years, without reforming the educational administration system, or even due to the sudden increase in funding and improper management and use, it is sufficient to completely bankrupt the educational spirit of a locality. The author believes that we should pay attention to two issues based on the current needs of education:

(1) Where should we look for the starting point for the implementation of the plans?

(2) From whom should we seek feedback on the implementation of the plans?

From the perspective of the plan itself, the content of the plan connects the central, provincial, and county education systems, including senior high, junior high, and primary education. None should be favored over the others. Naturally, the education administrations at all levels are responsible personnel. However, the most complex and difficult task is to promote the universality of education. After decades of efforts that have resulted in countless flaws, there is an urgent need for practical plans to rectify the situation or start anew. Other countries calculate the number of illiterate people in terms of per thousand, while we still hold onto the figure of per ten. The sooner education becomes universal, the sooner the country's status will improve. The education sector should currently devote all its efforts to universal education. For example, it would not be excessive to demand that the current plan give special attention to universal education.

The implementation of universal education has always been based on the county as a unit. The most important person responsible for implementing universal education is the county education bureau chief. If, after the plan is passed, the Ministry of Education transmits the plan regarding universal education to the Provincial Department of Education, which then transmits it to the County Education Bureau, and the County Education Bureau Chief still holds it without any solution and ultimately files it away, it would not only waste the efforts of many experts, but would also leave local education with no hope of revitalization. The fact that the Education Bureau Chiefs hold it without any solution should not solely be blamed on their lack of effort. There are many reasons for this, which can be listed as follows: 1. Lack of determination to make progress; 2. Too few and too poor support staff; 3. Funding constraints preventing bold advancement; 4. Lack of assistance from superiors; 5. Lack of cooperation within the education sector; 6. Disorderly teachers; 7. Interference from related organizations; 8. Local feudal forces creating obstacles in everything; 9. The individual himself is not satisfied with being the bureau chief, but only temporarily using it as a retreat or for recuperation; 10. Most of the time is spent on raising funds, resolving difficulties, and maintaining the status quo, leading to mental and physical exhaustion; 11. Lack of guidance, preventing them from taking action; 12. Fundamental lack of understanding of education; 13... and so on. To summarize, (1) the bureau chief is not the right person, (2) the organization is unsound, (3) the provincial education administrative agency fails to assume the responsibility of guidance and guarantee, and (4) the administrative power is too small, the scope of work is too complex, and the dual responsibilities of funding and operation are concentrated in one person.

Most local education exists in such a parasitic state. Excellent talents often give up after a slight attempt. Simply seeking to get through a year safely is already difficult, and even then, a certain amount of anxiety and hidden pain is inevitable. As a result, provincial education directors often feel that local education is too troublesome and difficult to manage. If such a state is not first eliminated and eradicated, and the implementation plan, which is related to the new life of future education, is lightly placed in such an environment, the result can be foreseen. Recalling the initial stages of local education in China, in a state of complete unpreparedness and lack of methods, the power of education was lightly taken over from the hands of successful candidates in the imperial examinations and even commoners. As a result, localities with the ability to run education were governed by the people themselves, and schools and villages were governed by themselves. Localities with weak economic capacity and cultural backwardness were happy to be uninvolved in both public and private matters. Three to five schools were established in a county of hundreds of miles as mere decorations. Now, all we see is the non-standard, deformed development, and the more backward becoming even more backward. How painful this is! To ensure that this plan does not become a mere formality, I fear that some paths for reforming local education administration must first be established.

1. The selection of leaders for local education administration: Observing the current situation, county education bureau chiefs are more likely to be competent in economically prosperous and culturally advanced areas. However, sometimes, due to the abundance of talent and the formation of various factions, improper appointment methods may still lead to disputes. This gives rise to two issues: the selection criteria and the method of appointment. From the perspective of legal evolution, the qualifications for bureau chiefs in the Education Bureau Regulations of 1923 have been significantly raised. However, for the sake of a law applicable throughout the country, the minimum standards cannot but be lowered, which affects the entire system. The current solution is for the central government to stipulate the minimum standards for each level of phased improvement, while each province formulates its own separate regulations. Without raising these qualifications and without restricting those who do not understand education, local education will be completely helpless. At the same time, the treatment should be commensurate with the qualifications and duties. Usually, the standards and treatment for bureau chiefs in small counties are low, which urgently needs to be corrected in the provincial administration. Small counties are in need of development and require the most capable talents, otherwise, they will forever lag behind. The appointment method also varies. The method of having the county magistrate recommend several people and the provincial education director select one person is the most meaningless and irresponsible. Some bureau chiefs are appointed through comparative selection, but what can be compared is only the evidence on paper, which is also unreliable. A more progressive method is, of course, the examination system, but what is tested is knowledge, not character and talent. If examinations are used as a preliminary selection, followed by a longer period of training and practice, it seems easier to find the right person. If the treatment is improved, this system may be feasible. After considerable observation and practice, the local concept of "must use local people" can be eliminated. This requires effort from the provincial administration.

2. Administrative expenses should not come from local education funds. The expenses of the Education Bureau have traditionally been paid out of the education fund, which is inevitably subject to proportional restrictions. Low salaries for bureau chiefs make it difficult to find the right person, and low salaries for bureau staff make it difficult to recruit them. The administrative operations themselves cannot be streamlined due to the lack of funds. Because the funds for local are derived from local areas, they are regarded as a local organziation. The province only having the right of appointment and removal makes active management difficult. The combination of administrative fees and operating expenses, with the same source of funding, is prone to abuse. In places where the funding is too low, such as a bureau chief's salary of 20 or 30 yuan a month, is clearly ridiculous. To avoid various difficulties, the administrative expenses of the Education Bureau should be paid from the provincial revenue. Only then can the administrative expenses and budgets be subject to strict periodic review. Increasing the annual expenditure by 300,000 to 400,000 yuan across the province will significantly help the educational spirit and administrative management. Even if it cannot be fully implemented for the time being, in places where funding is more difficult, no one will be willing to make fruitless sacrifices unless this is done. Alternatively, the province and county can each share half of the salaries and office expenses, as determined by the province, which is a more progressive approach than the current system where the province's management is only a formality. With the bureau chief appointed and paid by the province, and the management of local affairs, local obstacles and misunderstandings can be reduced and more easily understood. The salaries of bureau chiefs and staff can be effectively increased, allowing those who are dedicated to this work to support their families, reducing economic pressure and the temptation to change careers.

3. The provincial government should be responsible for local education funding. An education bureau chief with fundraising abilities is easily supported by the general public and trusted by superiors. Those with educational aspirations and knowledge but lacking accounting skills and acumen are often unsuccessful and leave. What a paradoxical phenomenon! Those engaged in education should fundamentally recognize that abolishing miscellaneous taxes is the way to alleviate the suffering of the people. However, on the one hand, they have to adopt the principle of collecting even the smallest amounts to scrape together funds to maintain current operations. Open up the education tax items of various counties and conduct an examination. If miscellaneous taxes are resolutely and strictly abolished, local education may immediately become completely bankrupt. What another paradoxical phenomenon! The provincial education administration treats local education as if it were allowing ragtag armies to forage everywhere and raise funds locally. As a result, the disputes, complexities, and malpractices arising from funding completely bury the educational spirit and meaning of a locality. The provincial government considers it a local issue and cannot have a thorough reform plan. The supervision, restrictions, admonitions, and prohibitions on paper are at most related to the individual bureau chief, but paper is ultimately just paper. Education bureau chiefs should ask more about education, but ask less about finance or social interaction. This way, talents can be more specialized and pure, and education itself can benefit from administrative efficiency. The provincial government should have a comprehensive management system for local education funding, which cannot be the sole responsibility of one or two staff members. If the education banking system is adopted, with branches in each locality, and formal banking procedures are used for deposits, withdrawals, interest, loans, and mortgages, most of the disputes or malpractices can be reduced. The audit aspect should have a dedicated processing agency to prevent bureau chiefs from covering up the situation and deceiving superiors. The source of funding should not be left to the local government to handle piecemeal. The provincial government should designate several major taxes as special funds for local education, and strict restrictions should be placed on the taxes freely collected by each county. At the same time, attention should be paid to the clearing and collection of local education assets. In short, education bureau chiefs should only be concerned with the distribution and restriction of expenditures, while the provincial government should be extremely responsible for the increase, collection, and custody of revenue, with precise procedures, plans, and specialized agencies and personnel. Let the "education bureau chief" devote their full energy to running "education" and help the "education bureau" quickly escape the era of the "education tax bureau."

4. The centralization of local education administrative power: In places where feudal forces are most entrenched, education bureau chiefs are like puppets. Each village has its own master, and the education bureau chief has no say in the modification of plans or the advancement or retirement of personnel. As for the observance of laws and regulations, the improvement of teaching, and the report of guidance, since the education bureau chief is not the master of education management, it is like the autumn wind blowing past the ears. The education bureau is equivalent to a dummy, only dealing with matters perfunctorily. The provincial government should grant the education bureau chief full authority and provide full protection and assistance within the framework of provincial principles and plans, so that local education does not remain parasitic on feudal forces forever. Of course, local education should cooperate with society and not harbor narrow-minded views. However, cooperation is cooperation, and interference is interference. During the period of political tutelage, to hope that excellent bureau chiefs will be appointed to reorganize local education, the entire enterprise should be fully entrusted before it can be started. In order to complete the degree of local autonomy as soon as possible, the provincial administrative authorities should first decide on their attitude. If they are determined to reform, they should find ways to do so fundamentally.

5. The issue of teacher consolidation: The disorder of local teachers is self-evident. However, the responsibility for the disorder should be borne by the past education administrative authorities. The quantity of teachers required for their promotion of education was not commensurate with the need. They had no precise standards and procedures for selecting teachers, they had no power to interfere with landowning principals who appointed unqualified teachers, they had no way to train new teachers, and they had no way to ensure that in-service teachers improved and did not fall behind. In the end, intentionally or unintentionally, year after year, they filled the education sector with unqualified teachers. This is not the fault of the teachers. Those who are unqualified are not retained here, and there are other places for them to be retained. They do not necessarily have to be teachers. Even if they are willing to be teachers, if the restrictions are stricter, they can make more preparations in advance. Those who are unqualified were already employed, and then they took inspection and other coercive measures to barely justify themselves. This is something that those of us who have been involved in education administration work should feel ashamed of. For the current consolidation, from the fundamental perspective, we hope that the education sector will pay serious attention to the issue of teacher training without being prejudiced. From the symptomatic perspective, due to the distribution of talents in each province, the standards for primary school teachers at each level should be stipulated in phases. Those who meet the minimum standards should strive to prove themselves and prepare to raise their rank within the effective period of their service. After several years of joint efforts to reach the standards set, each locality should not be allowed to appoint teachers below the prescribed standards. Of course, teacher consolidation is more complex than any other issue. The organization of provincial education administration should have a section dedicated to teacher issues, establish a consolidation plan for several years, and strictly implement it. With such assistance, education bureau chiefs will be comparatively more courageous in implementing their proposals.

The above points can be felt by comrades who care about local education. Of course, they may not agree on the solution. We hope that experienced education administrative authorities can pay more attention to this issue and study ways to solve it.

Educational Opinion (4) by Gao Junshan 85

(4) The evolution of clothing is not entirely accidental. It must be suitable for the national conditions in order to be established and sustainable. Western suits are suitable for the environment and equipment of Westerners. In China's environment, they are too thin in winter and too thick in summer. This is a common complaint among those who wear Western suits. Therefore, Western suits are not suitable for China's environment.

(5) Chinese clothing is very simple and easy to make beautiful. Western suits must be made of exquisite materials and good workmanship, and must be carefully maintained at all times to be presentable. If one or two Western suits are prepared and worn from the beginning to the end of the year, covered in oil and full of wrinkles, it is even more unsightly than unpretentious Chinese clothing.

(6) Chinese clothing is more convenient and does not take much effort to wear.

(7) Chinese clothing is more comfortable. The fact that many people who wear Western suits often change into Chinese clothing when they return home is clear evidence of this.

(2) Methods

(1) The Ministry of Education should issue a circular to all large, medium, and small schools across the country, strictly requiring them to use domestic materials to make domestic clothing, and instructing them to wear out their existing Western suits before no longer producing them.

National Scout Jamboree (Chinese Photography)

(2) The Ministry of Education should instruct the principals and deans of students in each school to be responsible for supervising and encouraging students, and to encourage each other among colleagues and classmates to implement this ministerial order.

(3) Local education administrative agencies should send personnel to investigate the extent to which large, medium, and small schools are making efforts to implement this circular, and commend and commend them to show encouragement.

(4) Schools should be responsible for social publicity.

(5) Staff of education administrative agencies at all levels should lead by example.

(Note 1) Domestic clothing is a collective term for long and short garments.

(Note 2) Using domestic goods to make domestic clothing does not mean wearing uniforms.

(Note 3) If domestic clothing is inconvenient or does not meet the principles of hygiene and beauty, it can still be fully improved, but it should not imitate the clothing of any other country.

▲School flags, emblems, school songs,

slogans, etc. should all use domestic

language

(1) Reasons

(1) An independent country has its own language and writing to express itself. Looking at schools today (especially universities), Western languages are often regarded as fashionable. The slogans, school flags, emblems, and even the slogans on sports caps and sports clothing sometimes use purely Western languages. Even the school songs sung at the closing ceremony and the slogans shouted during sports sometimes use English. This purely Westernized practice is truly heartbreaking. We often deplore the invasion of Eastern and Western cultures, but these kinds of actions are not invasions by others; they are simply accepting them wholeheartedly and rejecting our own country's language to use the language of others. This is not only losing the national identity, but also incurring the ridicule of foreigners.

(2) Methods

The Ministry of Education should issue a circular to the education departments of each province, instructing all schools to replace all Western-language slogans, school flags, school emblems, school songs, slogans, etc. with domestic language. (To be continued)

Third Day of National Scout General Inspection 86

Performances held... Visited the Mausoleum Today

Yesterday was the third day of the National Scout General Inspection. The sky was clear and bright, and various groups held performances in the afternoon. Dai Jitao also gave a speech to the Scouts of Jiangsu and Zhejiang provinces. This morning, they visited the mausoleum of Generalissimo Sun Yat-sen and held a memorial week. The situation is recorded below:

Camp Situation 87

Since there was news of the cancellation of the large-scale camp earlier, the preparation for the large-scale camp was relatively negligent. The sudden announcement of the camp on the 17th must have been made in haste. After one night's allocation, the situation gradually became ready during the lighting of thousands of lamps, truly a grand occasion. The camp area was originally planned to be surrounded to maintain order more easily, but due to budgetary reasons, it could not be done. Therefore, the camp area was abnormally chaotic. Fortunately, the Scouts of each group were experienced and built fences to divide and guard the area. Visitors were amazed and admired. Among them, several groups built beautiful words with branches, which is worthy of praise and truly a lively manifestation of the children's heaven.

Afternoon Performances 88

▲Performance Scenarios

At 2:00 PM on the 20th, performances were held in two venues, the officer training hall and the platoon division area. Scout curriculum demonstrations were given. Dai Jitao, Zhang Daofan, Chen Lifu, Sike Batu, and other guests, totaling over ten thousand spectators, attended. The performances included over ten categories: drills, climbing, semaphore signaling, camping, first aid, cycling, human pyramids, message signaling, bridge building, fire starting, knot tying, national martial arts, military band, and firefighting. Scout troops actively participated, demonstrating agility and coordination, garnering audience praise. The event concluded late in the evening. Detailed results are still being compiled.

Yesterday's performance began at 3:00 PM, by troop unit. The program and a list of participating troop names are recorded below:

(2) Troop Yells, Troop Sounds, Troop Signals: Troop 73

(3) Climbing: Troops 48, 108, 81, 15, 177

(4) Bridge Building: Troops 5, 15

(6) Semaphore: Troops 119, 57, 148, 5, 15, 196, 78, 127

Dai Jitao's Address 89

| Dai and His Wife Inspect Barracks |

| Speech to the Liangjiang Boy Scouts: |

▲The Two Most Important Words in Life Are Courtesy and Righteousness

▲Parents, Teachers, and Friends Are Crucial to One's Lifelong Career

▲Adhere to Tenets and Embrace a Spirit of Sacrifice

At 2:00 PM on the 20th, Dai Fu-xian, Chairman of the general inspection and grand encampment, accompanied by his wife, inspected the scouts' residences and offices, and toured the barracks. They saw many children cooking and preparing fragrant dishes. Dai smiled and said, "This food smells really good!" At this time, Lu Lihua, principal of Liangjiang Girls' School, invited him to give a speech to the school's scouts. Dai agreed and delivered a speech, stating: "Brothers, my throat is sore today, and my voice is not clear. Please forgive me. What I want to say to you, I already said at the assembly the day before yesterday, and now I will say it again: The two most important words in life are courtesy and righteousness. These two words, courtesy and righteousness, should not be interpreted in a pedantic way. By courtesy, we mean the organization of human society, and by righteousness, we mean social action. If these two words are lost, the nation will inevitably decline. The Chinese have made this mistake. Therefore, Chinese boy scouts must revitalize these two words. Furthermore, the decline of Chinese women's education and the weakness of their bodies are self-evident. They naturally suffer everywhere when undertaking social endeavors. However, in education, there are four major things related to one's lifelong career: father, mother, teacher, and friends. Education is evident everywhere in the habits of our people. A father picks up two big eyes and a stick – this is the father's education. A mother offers her breasts. A teacher, like the old-fashioned tutors, has treasures in his hands – roasted chestnuts, candy, slaps, and a wooden stick. Friends deceive each other. This is the education of teachers and friends. With social education like this, how can China not be weak? Moreover, only one-tenth of the Chinese people have received education, and even fewer are women. The number of women serving as girl scouts is even smaller. However, the responsibility of promoting the girl scout movement rests on your shoulders. Do not think that wearing scout uniforms and hats makes you scouts, forgetting your great responsibility. Therefore, I hope that you will spread the good education you have received from your parents, teachers, and friends, and take on the responsibility of creating a new China based on the Three Principles of the People. In particular, you must abide by the scout tenets, embrace courage and a spirit of sacrifice, serve the country, and serve society. You must transform more girls in the villages into scouts, and that will be the success of your mission." Finally, Principal Lu Lihua of the school gave thanks, and the event concluded.

Business Discussion Meeting 90

The Boy Scout business discussion meeting opened yesterday morning, with Shi Weihuan chairing. He first reported the purpose of the meeting, followed by discussions on general Boy Scouts, Girl Scouts, the organization and training of existing (Rover) Scouts, and how to promote scouting in rural areas. The result was a decision to distribute opinion forms for service personnel to complete and submit to the Chinese Boy Scout Headquarters by the end of May. The Headquarters will compile the various opinions and publish them in newspapers and newsletters.

Morning Visit to the Mausoleum 91

▲Departure at 7:00 AM

The Boy Scouts will visit the mausoleum tomorrow, the 21st. Dai Jitao and the office have sent letters to the mausoleum management office, and permission has been granted for a full opening. All Boy Scouts are scheduled to depart for the mausoleum at 7:00 AM on the 21st and hold a memorial week and social gathering in front of Sun Yat-sen's Mausoleum.

▲Mausoleum Visit Ceremony: 1. Stand at attention; 2. Play music; 3. Sing the Party Song; 4. Present wreaths (play music); 5. Bow three times to Sun Yat-sen's tomb; 6. The officiating priest respectfully reads Sun Yat-sen's will, with the entire group reciting aloud; 7. Three minutes of silence; 8. Sing the Boy Scout song; 9. Pay respects to the remains; 10. Play music; 11. Ceremony concludes.

▲Memorial Week Order: 1. All stand at attention; 2. Sing the Party Song; 3. Bow three times to the Party flag, national flag, and Sun Yat-sen's portrait; 4. The chairman respectfully reads Sun Yat-sen's will, with the entire group reciting aloud; 5. Three minutes of silence; 6. Report; 7. Ceremony concludes.

▲Funny Stories During the Heavy Rain

During the heavy rain on the 19th, some groups took shelter in the camp, while others went to the camp to get raincoats. In the midst of this chaos, three or five Boy Scouts played pranks, taking the opportunity to steal other people's leather shoes, causing a few boy and girl scouts to become barefoot immortals for a while. Also, the camp ropes were like a net, and if you were not careful, you would trip over them, so many mud bodhisattvas were added to the ranks of the barefoot immortals. Moreover, some people slept soundly and were not disturbed by the heavy rain until they woke up and realized the trouble the rain had caused.

Important News 94

Recent Developments in the Jiangsu Provincial People's Education Institute Experimental Zone 95

Since its establishment, the Huangxiang Experimental Zone of the Jiangsu Provincial People's Education Institute has spared no effort in promoting various educational facilities within the zone. A summary of the zone's recent work is recorded below:

(1) Implementing Compulsory Literacy: After the conclusion of the first phase of the zone's people's schools, in order to achieve literacy for all people in the zone, the Improvement Conference decided to implement compulsory literacy starting in March of this year. All residents of the zone between the ages of twelve and twenty must attend people's schools. Those who are absent without reason for one week must pay a "foolish people" fine of 30 cents of silver. The Township Office submitted this measure to the county government for record. The Wuxi County Government also sent a literacy police officer to be stationed in the zone for a long time to persuade and guide. The program has been implemented for almost two months and the results are very impressive. Almost all those who should attend people's schools attend every day to learn to read.

(2) Organizing Mobile Teaching: For residents of the zone who are over twenty years old and not within the compulsory age range, and who cannot attend people's schools due to household chores and other constraints, the zone's staff compiles mobile teaching materials and goes to the farmhouses in turn every day at 4:00 PM to conduct individual teaching, but it is not compulsory. More than seventy people in the zone are receiving this education, mostly women. The oldest of them is fifty years old, and she is also studying diligently to learn to read, which is admirable.

(3) Establishing Nurseries: This semester, the zone established a nursery, renting two civilian houses as the site. There are 20 children, aged four to six, who are cared for in the nursery. The zone's female staff are responsible for guiding them.

(4) Guiding Township Offices: The zone's staff guides the township office in carrying out various local autonomy tasks within the zone, such as household registration, neighborhood selection, road construction, and banning gambling and smoking. Members of the Improvement Association are even more enthusiastic in assisting and participating in everything.

(5) Conducting Monthly Household Cleanliness Inspections: In addition to the People's Hospital clinic providing daily medical consultations for residents and organizing health campaigns and promoting various sports, the zone also conducts monthly household cleanliness inspections on the 15th of each month. The four items of the bedroom are inspected, and guidance is provided at any time. Those with excellent results are given honorary awards at public gatherings. As a result, household cleanliness has greatly improved compared to before.

(6) Holding the Second Children's Health Competition: On the 17th and 18th of this month, the zone held the second children's health competition, with more than 70 children participating. The inspection items were divided into two categories: physical condition and medical aspects. Each participating child received a gift bag of candy. Two children in each age group from one to six also received four or five practical prizes each. An awards ceremony was held on the evening of the second day, accompanied by various children's health promotions and entertainment.

(7) Editing Various Teaching Materials and Reports: The various people's school teaching materials edited by the zone, such as the People's Reader, which is a mixed compilation of party principles, literacy, and common sense, People's Songs, People's Calligraphy Practice Books, and People's Small Series, are widely promoted. The People's Reader has recently been reprinted, with sales reaching more than 5,000 copies. Regarding the first year of experimentation, the book "Huangxiang Experimental Zone" was specially edited, recording everything in great detail. The price is 40 cents per copy.

Fudan Will Offer a Summer Term National Defense Chemistry Specialty 97

▲Studying Military Poison Gas

▲Strengthening Borders and Defending Against Foreign Aggression

Lin Jiyong, the dean of the science department of Fudan University in Shanghai, believes that with the current global war clouds, future wars will surely break out. The United States, Britain, France, Germany, Japan, and other countries are spending vast amounts of money to vigorously explore military poison gases. Our country's national defense is lax, and there is no preparation whatsoever, which is a major danger. Last autumn, he added a military chemistry course, hiring Han Zukang and others as professors, and produced seven kinds of chemical weapons, which were publicly demonstrated, with satisfactory results. This was the first time this had happened in universities across the country, as has been reported in various newspapers. It is now known that the school, in order to strengthen the borders, defend against foreign aggression, and cultivate self-defense talents, will offer a "Summer Term National Defense Chemistry Specialty" this summer, from July 1st to August 9th, for a total of six weeks. Each week will consist of 24 hours of lectures and practice. The courses offered include: Introduction to Poison Gas, Explosive Chemistry, Calculation of Explosive Power, Poison Gas Manufacturing, Poison Gas Tactics, Research on Smoke Screens and Incendiary Devices, Protective Masks, Explosive Manufacturing, and Poison Gas Testing Methods. Admission qualifications: Anyone with a letter of introduction from a school or public institution who passes the entrance examination will be admitted. Those who complete the course and pass the examination will be issued a certificate. The enrollment quota is set at 50 people, and no more will be accepted when the quota is full. The prospectus is being printed. The important reasons for the school's offering of the National Defense Chemistry Specialty are as follows: (1) Although the history of chemical warfare is only a little over ten years, the diligence with which various countries research and the number of inventions are amazing. Although the Hague Peace Conference explicitly prohibited the use of poison gas by belligerent countries in 1899, when the European War broke out, each country acted in its own interests, and the use of poison gas increased. The Hague Treaty was just a formality. (2) We must recognize that national defense chemistry is a protector, not a destroyer. We must research the properties of various poison gases and their antidotes, and the manufacturing methods of anti-gas equipment, in order to protect the soldiers fighting for the country on the battlefield. We must research the manufacturing methods of smoke screens to prevent enemy aircraft from attacking, so that public buildings and cultural institutions in the country can be spared from destruction. (3) No citizen with a sense of national defense does not want to study this subject in order to resist foreign aggression. The school gave a performance last winter, which attracted the attention of military, political, and academic circles across the country. Therefore, in-depth research should be conducted to make a contribution.

Qunzhi University's Request to the Ministry of Education 98

Shanghai Qunzhi University, founded nearly ten years ago, has had considerable achievements. However, last autumn, after a change of leadership, some students withdrew from the school. The Ministry of Education has reportedly heard about this and has issued a notice to suspend the school during the summer term. It is now reported that the school has convened a meeting of school directors stationed in Shanghai and has drafted a concrete plan to strive for perfection. They have jointly requested the Ministry of Education to revoke its decision. The school's student union has also sent representatives to the Shanghai Education Bureau to explain the events of last year's upheaval and the school's current situation, and to request the Education Bureau to forward the request to the Ministry of Education, requesting that it be maintained in order to preserve academic pursuits.

李彥士定期放洋 111

▲ Representative to the World Power Conference

▲ Publicly Recommended by the Federation of Private Electrical Enterprises

▲ Departing by Ship on the 29th of This Month

The Second World Power Conference is about to be held in Germany. The Chinese government has appointed three representatives to attend. One of them is Mr. Huang Boqiao, the director of the Shanghai Public Utilities Bureau, who set sail on the 15th of this month, as previously reported. The Federation of Private Electrical Enterprises has also nominated two representatives. One of them is Mr. Li Yanshi, an electrical entrepreneur, who is scheduled to depart for Germany on the 29th of this month aboard the Derfflinger. Mr. Li is a senior student who studied in Germany and Austria and has held important government positions. He was originally a legal expert but, recognizing that China's industry and commerce were underdeveloped and that the electrical industry was the foundation for developing various industries, he devoted himself to electrical engineering. He pioneered China's first long-distance power transmission project, the Zhenhua Electrical Machinery Manufacturing Plant, and was the first to promote agricultural irrigation projects. To this day, production has increased in the Changzhou and Wuxi areas, and farmers have benefited from this. Recently, he has been running the electricity business in his hometown of Huzhou with great success. The chairman of this Second World Power Conference, which will be held in the German capital, Mr. Kou Degen, came to China last year and met with Mr. Li, personally inviting him to attend. Recently, he sent another telegram urging Mr. Li to attend, stating that the conference will discuss various electrical regulations and that Mr. Li, as a legal expert, would be indispensable. Therefore, Mr. Li had no choice but to reluctantly accept the public recommendation of the Federation of Electrical Enterprises and go to Germany to attend. It is believed that Mr. Li's participation in this conference will contribute greatly to solving legal issues related to public utilities around the world.

保存舊有擋案之訓令 114

The Shanghai Special Municipality Government received an order from the Executive Yuan yesterday, stating that the National Beiping Research Institute had sent a letter stating that the old files stored in various provinces and cities were of great importance to historical research materials. If they were not specially preserved, it was feared that they would disappear over time. It requested that the matter be presented to the Executive Yuan and then to the National Government, ordering all agencies in various provinces, cities, and counties to properly preserve the old files or hand them over to academic institutions for preservation and organization, and not to destroy them arbitrarily. The ministry found that the files in various provinces, cities, and counties were of great importance to institutions and cultural relics. All materials that could be used for historical research should be cataloged and carefully preserved. The institute's request was not without merit. The original letter should be copied and presented to the Executive Yuan and then to the National Government, ordering all agencies in provinces, cities, and counties across the country to comply with it for the sake of public convenience. The case was then forwarded to the Executive Yuan, which was then submitted to the National Government with the instruction that all documents were understood and had been submitted to the 66th National Affairs Conference for deliberation and approval. The order was issued to the Executive Yuan for compliance. In addition to the separate orders, the government was ordered to comply immediately and instruct its subordinates to comply with it as a whole.

中東問題中郵件損失 115

▲ Russian Diplomatic Committee Refuses

The Directorate General of Posts previously reported that the postmaster of Jilin and Heilongjiang reported that the mail coming and going from the post offices in the area, along with the mail carriers, either on ships or on the way, had been robbed by the Soviet army, and many of the mail items delivered to the Russian post office via the Ussuri Railway had not been received to this day. The Directorate General of Posts then submitted a request to the Ministry of Communications and forwarded it to the Ministry of Foreign Affairs for negotiation. The bureau recently received an instruction from the Ministry of Communications, which stated that the Ministry of Foreign Affairs had replied that the German Embassy in China had stated that the case had been negotiated with the Russian government but had been rejected by the Russian Diplomatic Committee. The reason given was that the claims made by China were within the territory of the three eastern provinces. The Ministry of Foreign Affairs of Russia meant that the case should be negotiated directly with the Soviet representative in Harbin by the Chinese authorities. In addition to ordering the Jilin Special Envoy to comply, a corresponding consultation was requested for verification.

欵產處調查貧户 116

▲ Rice Subsidies to Be Issued on May 1st

County Chief Leng of Shanghai County, seeing that rice prices have been rising recently and people are finding it difficult to eat, sent a special letter to the Property Management Office to organize a fair price for rice. Subsequently, the office decided to subsidize the price of rice, according to the method of the ninth year of the Republic, giving money instead of grain, and replied to the county government for approval. It is now learned that the county government has decided to start the program on May 1st. The Property Management Office believes that the deadline is approaching and immediately sent letters to the district chiefs, urging them to quickly investigate and verify the extremely poor households within their jurisdictions and report back within a few days so that subsidies can be issued separately.

吳淞朱區長明日乘艦出巡各汛地 117

Zhu Bingzheng, the fourth district chief of the Wusong Water Police, in order to inspect overseas defenses and strive for reforms, has perfected the internal affairs of the district headquarters in recent days.
