國際貿易問題講演紀 118

▲ Observing China's National Economy from the Perspective of Import and Export Trade

At 3 p.m. yesterday, the Shanghai YMCA held its seventh academic lecture, given by Dr. Shou Yicheng. The following is a summary of his speech:

There should be two types of liquidation in China's national economy: one is domestic liquidation, and the other is international liquidation. From the perspective of domestic liquidation, (1) scarce production, (2) large consumption, (3) leisurely production, and (4) rapid consumption are the most common phenomena in China's current economic sphere. In other words, in terms of production, no industry is backward, and in terms of consumption, no matter is forward. The result of the liquidation is always negative rather than positive, and deficient rather than surplus. If we look at the liquidation in international trade, it has been 66 years since the third year of Tongzhi (i.e., 1864). Among them, exports exceeded imports in only six years: 1864, 1872, 1873, 1874, 1875, and 1878. In the remaining 60 years, imports exceeded exports in every year. This is the first pathological condition. Foreign markets are shrinking by leaps and bounds, and the power of foreign merchants is permeating the hinterland. This is the second pathological condition. Export merchants lack sufficient capital and lack sound organization. This is the third pathological condition. The development of international trade depends on the agility of international finance. China lacks incentives for export trade credit guarantee systems, and the international exchange business is mostly controlled by foreign banks. This is the fourth pathological condition. Whether the ocean transportation industry is developed or not is closely related to the expansion of foreign trade. In China, foreign transportation and marine insurance businesses have either died prematurely or have not yet sprouted. This is the fifth pathological condition. Protectionist trade policies are a necessary means to encourage the development of domestic infant industries. In China, however, tariffs and miscellaneous taxes are everywhere, and export excise taxes, which are explicitly prohibited by the U.S. Constitution, are regarded as an important source of revenue in China. Economic suicide cannot be avoided. This is the sixth pathological condition. Trading in good faith has been China's old tradition. However, in recent times, export merchants only seek immediate, temporary benefits and disregard the credit of various industries abroad. Adulteration and forgery are ubiquitous, so that Chinese merchants, who were once known for their credit, have become unscrupulous elements with falling credit in international trade. Moral bankruptcy is the ultimate bottom line. This is the seventh pathological condition. All countries in international trade try their best to avoid the disadvantages of passive trade and indirect trade and aim at achieving automatic trade and direct trade as a common goal. China is passive and passive, indirect and indirect. Therefore, it is nominally foreign trade, but in reality, it is trade with foreign firms or trade with compradors. Oppression, aggression, exploitation, and fraud are ubiquitous, and the most severely affected are export merchants or farmers and workers who have a close relationship with export trade. They are shortsighted, ignorant, and unable to extricate themselves from harming the country and harming the community. This is the eighth pathological condition. All of the above are important reasons why China's export trade cannot be fully developed. However, the scientific study of international trade should first be based on facts. Therefore, we will compare and analyze the past and present development of import and export trade over the past 60 years in order to adapt to the trend and strive to

The current situation and trends of China's international trade can be roughly divided into the following points for discussion: (1) Observing from the total value of trade, China's total international trade volume was 843 million Customs Taels in the first year of the Republic of China, and 2.423 billion Taels in the eighteenth year, an increase of more than three times. This cannot but be considered a considerable improvement. (2) Observing from the amount of trade deficit, since the opening of the sea ban, trade deficit has become common. Since the establishment of the Republic of China, the amount of trade deficit has been increasing year by year. From the first year of the Republic to the eighteenth year, there was no year without a trade deficit. However, it decreased slightly during the European War. In the eighth year of the Republic, the trade deficit fell to 16 million Taels, which was a rare good phenomenon in the last 40 years. It is a pity. This cannot but be considered one aspect of the unhealthy state of the national economy. (3) Observing from the changes in important export commodities, the position of China's important export commodities in international trade, if viewed from a vertical historical perspective, was initially tea, followed by raw silk, and recently by soybeans. Since 1864, with relevant records available, the general outline can be listed as follows, with ten years as a period, divided into six periods, and with the position of export goods in recent years following them.

Year 1 2 3 4 5 6 7 Notes

1873 Tea Raw Silk Cotton Soybeans

1883 Tea Raw Silk Cotton Soybeans

1893 Tea Raw Silk Cotton Soybeans

1903 Raw Silk Tea Cotton Soybeans (A) Eggs Peanuts (A) Refers to the number in 1904

1913 Raw Silk Soybeans Tea Cotton Peanuts (B) Tung Oil Eggs (B) Refers to the number in 1914

1923 Raw Silk Soybeans Cotton Tea Eggs Tung Oil Peanuts

1925 Raw Silk Soybeans Cotton Eggs Tea Tung Oil Peanuts

1927 Soybeans Raw Silk Cotton Tea Eggs Tung Oil Peanuts

1928 Soybeans Raw Silk Tea Eggs Cotton Tung Oil Peanuts

From the table on the right, we can see the possibility of development of various items in export trade. However, the increase in soybean production is mostly due to the Japanese management of the eastern provinces. Therefore, it is not enough to be deeply gratified. The two major export commodities of tea and silk, which have always been famous in the world, are now overwhelmed by Ceylon tea and Japanese silk. This is a true economic national shame that cannot be denied. (4) Observing from the supply and demand of important commodities, the import of cotton cloth has always ranked first in import trade. The second is either sugar, rice, wool, or cotton yarn. The import of rice has been increasing year by year, which is a strong proof of the lack of food and the decline of agriculture in our country. It is also sufficient to show that the food problem needs to be solved urgently. The gradual decrease in the import of cotton yarn is due to the change to the import of fine yarn and the development of foreign companies operating yarn factories in China. However, the development of the domestic yarn industry is also one of the important reasons. Furthermore, observing the import trade statistics for the 17th year of the Republic of China, the import value (A) was over 100 million Taels for cotton goods, (B) 90 million Taels for sugar (this is the highest number in recent years and a new record in the history of China's import trade), (C) over 60 million Taels for cotton, metals, minerals, and kerosene, (D) over 40 million Taels for wool products, (E) over 30 million Taels for candles, tobacco, flour, and chemical products, (F) over 20 million Taels for grains, paper, silk products, fish, seafood, cigarettes, hemp, and coal, (G) over 10 million Taels for machinery, wood, meat products, cotton yarn, dyes, synthetic indigo, and leather. These can all be produced in China or can be replaced by domestic products. However, due to frequent internal strife, bankruptcy of all industries, poor technology, and difficult odds, there are cases where foreign goods are used to replace domestic goods, while there are few cases where domestic goods are used to replace foreign goods. If all sectors of the national economy can strive to "replace foreign goods," then promoting domestic goods will have practical significance, and it will be a matter of course to transform the trade deficit into a trade surplus. (5) Observing from the export trade of various industrial products, China's foreign trade has been exporting raw materials and importing foreign goods for many years, which has become a fixed pattern. The export of industrial products can be said to be minimal. However, in recent years, the export of machine-made foreign goods has increased significantly, which seems to be part of the evidence of the progress of domestic manufacturing. During the 14th year of the Republic of China, the total value of machine-made foreign goods exported was over 2.2748 million Taels. In the 15th year, it was over 26.656 million Taels. In the 17th year, it was 39.57 million Taels, an increase of about ten times. The increase in the export of this kind of foreign-style machine-made goods can prove that China's products have gradually occupied a minimum level of power in overseas markets. It can also be seen that this industry has gradually tended to develop. However, among these export goods, some are transported to Hong Kong and then re-enter China from Hong Kong. Some are manufactured by factories set up by foreign merchants in China, so we cannot but pay attention to them. (6) Observing from the import trade of special industrial products, the machinery in China's industrial products has always been supplied by foreign countries. Therefore, the number of machinery imports each year can be said to be a barometer of China's industrial progress. During the second year of the Republic of China, the import of machinery was valued at just over 4.65 million Taels. In the eighth year, it increased to 14 million Taels. In the tenth year, the highest number was over 55 million Taels. Recently, it is still over 19 million Taels. All of these situations can be used as a standard for estimating the rise and fall of China's industry. However, there are many foreigners who have set up factories in China, and the machinery purchased and used by foreign factories must also account for an important part of it. Therefore, it cannot be used as the only standard for China's industrial progress. (7) Observing from the source of intangible exports, a trade deficit is not always detrimental to a country's economy. Take the United Kingdom as an example. There is hardly a year without a trade deficit. In 1926, it was 470 million pounds, and in 1929, it was 366 million pounds. However, the United Kingdom's national wealth does not seem to be damaged. The intangible exports of the United Kingdom are of great value, such as ship freight, interest on foreign investment, commissions, and insurance premiums. China has an annual trade deficit, but there is a huge amount of silver imported every year. In the past two years, the amount has been over 100 million Taels. The reason for this is that remittances from overseas Chinese to their homeland are the most important source. They use investment to enrich their country, and we use labor to alleviate our poverty. Although the labor and leisure are different, and the work is different, they are governed by the principle of adapting to the environment. The amount of foreign investment in China is also huge, and attention should be paid to it. These imports that are not seen in the customs registers are mutually causal with China's various tangible export trades and are closely related. (8) Observing from the destination of tangible imports, in the early years of Daoguang in the former Qing Dynasty, import and export trade was concentrated in Guangdong. During the reign of Daoguang and Xianfeng, it gradually extended to the treaty ports along the Yangtze River, such as Shanghai and Hankou. After 1893, Tianjin and Niuzhuang gradually became important. After 1903, Jiaozhou and Dalian gradually emerged, and Harbin's market in land international trade became increasingly important. The shift in the situation is generally centered on the development of new transportation facilities such as roads and waterways. As transportation becomes more convenient, the production industry progresses. As the production industry progresses, the people's purchasing power increases. As the people's purchasing power increases, the destination of tangible imports expands. The situation is natural and difficult to resist. What should be repeatedly added to the meaning is that whether to import or not should be determined by whether we need it or not. Whether to give up or take, the power is in our own hands. Why should we allow foreign goods to overwhelm domestic goods, so that a good market becomes the tail of another country's industry? (9) Observing from the position of the total international trade volume of various countries, we can further observe China's position in the world's international trade. Before the European War (1912), the United Kingdom was definitely in the first place, Germany was in the second place, and the United States was in the third place. After the war, this situation fundamentally changed. The United States has jumped to the first place in global trade, and the United Kingdom has retreated to the second place, followed by Germany, France, Canada, India, Japan, Italy, Argentina, Belgium, and other countries. As for China, the amount it occupies in the world's trading arena was slightly higher in 1927, ranking ninth, compared to the twelfth place before the war. However, what we should pay attention to is that global trade has increased significantly after the war compared to before the war. The ratio of 37.797 trillion Gold Yuan in 1927 to 26.800 trillion Gold Yuan in 1913 means that 1927 increased by nearly 70 percent. Under this situation of rapid increase in world trade, China's international trade is bound to keep pace, but it is still considered that the progress is too late and too slow. (10) Observing from the average trade volume per capita in proportion to the population of various countries, from the actual figures of international trade,

Page 14

Observation, China always ranks 12th in the world. If we observe from the proportion of population, China is indeed always at the bottom of the world in every year. According to the statistics of the League of Nations, the largest average trade volume per capita in the world is Aden, with more than 800 Gold Yuan per capita, followed by the British Malaya Archipelago, New Zealand, Canada, Australia, the Netherlands, Switzerland, and Newfoundland, with an average of more than 200 Yuan per capita. The average trade volume per capita in the United Kingdom is 188.88 Gold Yuan, Belgium is 171.88 Gold Yuan, France is 92.58 Gold Yuan, Germany is 74.61 Gold Yuan, the United States is 76.13 Gold Yuan, Japan is 33.27 Gold Yuan, and China's average trade volume per capita is only 2.96 Gold Yuan, the least among all countries. China can indeed be proud of its large population, but is it not too much of a disadvantage in terms of trade in proportion to the population?

From the above, we can see that if China's international trade is to be fully developed, the ways to focus on are roughly as follows: First, the implementation of protectionist trade policies. After the war, the governments of Europe and the United States all regarded encouraging export trade as the only policy to restore economic strength. Therefore, they spared no effort in protecting and encouraging basic industries. The Chinese government has repeatedly ordered the abolition of tariffs and miscellaneous taxes, and it is bound to be implemented. Policies to reduce and exempt export taxes, appropriately increase import taxes on special manufactured goods, and protect emerging industries and encourage export trade have also been planned by the authorities. This is what the government should strive to do. Second, countries engaged in international trade generally have strong capital and sound organization. China's economy is immature, and it is not easy to follow suit for a while. However, in order to compete in the international commercial arena, those engaged in international trade must be first-class entrepreneurs, and sound organization is a necessary condition for the success of foreign trade. This is what export merchants should strive to do themselves. Third, the auxiliary institutions of international trade are established by the government and by private individuals. It is generally recognized that they are necessary for the development of foreign trade. China already has a clue about the establishment of international exchange banks, export commodity inspection agencies, industrial and commercial visiting agencies, and commercial commissioners stationed in restaurants. However, the organization of auxiliary institutions such as the International Trade Research Committee and the National Export Trade Association, as well as the solution of problems such as increasing the convenience of international transportation, are still to be awaited in the near future. This is what the auxiliary institutions should strive to do. If Chinese youths can clarify the issue of export trade development as a matter of life and death for China's economic sector and can contribute to the scientific research of international commerce and the psychological construction of developing foreign trade movements, then it will be the blessing of the future of the national economy.

The Shanghai General Chamber of Commerce Telegraphed Request for Reduction of Silk Tax in Zhejiang Province 119

The Shanghai General Chamber of Commerce telegraphed the Zhejiang Provincial Government regarding the request for reduction of silk tax in Zhejiang Province: "To the esteemed Zhejiang Provincial Government in Hangzhou: On the 17th of this month, we received a letter from the Shanghai Silk Industry Branch stating, 'We believe that the weight of tax rates and the price of goods are inherently causally linked. In recent years, the silk industry in Hangzhou has suffered repeated blows from foreign-made products, struggling to defend itself. At the same time, foreign merchants in the Shanghai concessions are also using the shield of their tariff agreements to further seize the leadership of China's silk trade. Therefore, silk fabrics produced within the Shanghai concessions are exempt from taxation on both raw materials and finished products. Even when transported and sold inland, they only need to pay a light sub-port tax. From this point of view, considering the weight of the burden, it is self-evident that the cost of silk fabrics in Shanghai and Hangzhou is inevitably different. Consequently, the competitive power between the two is also clearly different. In this situation, if we want to save the decline of the Hangzhou silk industry, the only way is to quickly abolish the silk tax, just like in the Shanghai concessions. We are attaching a comparative table of silk fabric tax rates in Hangzhou, Suzhou, and Shanghai for your reference. We dare to ask for your attention and assistance so that the silk industry and commerce in Hangzhou and Shanghai can bear the tax burden at a uniformly average ratio, which will not only revive the declining silk industry in Zhejiang but also deeply benefit the national economy and people's livelihood.' A comparative table was attached to the letter. After checking the silk fabric tax rates in Suzhou, Hangzhou, and Shanghai listed in the table, Hangzhou's rate is the highest, followed by Suzhou, and then Shanghai. Comparing the differences, for each piece of silk fabric, the largest difference is 2 yuan per piece compared to Suzhou goods, and almost 3 yuan compared to Shanghai goods. The smallest difference is more than half a yuan compared to Suzhou goods, and more than 1 yuan and 3 jiao compared to Shanghai goods. Even if factory wages and other expenses are higher in Shanghai than in Hangzhou, Suzhou and Hangzhou are adjacent, and their economic conditions are similar. However, the tax rates in Suzhou and Hangzhou, based on the four items examined, differ by as much as 2 yuan, 1 yuan and 7 jiao, and 1 yuan and half a yuan per piece. The major reason for the drastic decline of the Hangzhou silk industry in recent years is the excessively heavy tax burden. The unemployment of workers and the prevalence of vagrants are enough to cause hidden worries, and the closure of silk crepe factories has led to a sharp decline in production. Although the tax rate has been increased, the tax revenue will inevitably decrease, which is detrimental to public finances. In our humble opinion, even if the Hangzhou silk tax rate cannot be the same as Shanghai's, it should be proportional to Suzhou's to avoid unequal treatment. Otherwise, the negative consequences may lead to the gradual relocation of the Hangzhou silk market to the Shanghai concessions, allowing foreigners to enjoy the benefit of chasing away birds from the bush, while Hangzhou loses the source of livelihood for hundreds of thousands of people, which is not a good plan. Therefore, we do not hesitate to bother you and submit the comparative table of tax amounts, requesting your esteemed government to review and consider it for implementation, which is truly for the public benefit. The Shanghai Special Municipality Merchant Groups Reorganization Committee bows. Xiao."

Difficulties in Recruiting Labor for Road Construction in Baoshan 120

▲ Various Public Organizations Submit a Petition to the Construction Department Requesting Flexible Handling

Since Baoshan received the instruction from the Jiangsu Provincial Construction Department to implement labor recruitment for road construction, the Construction Bureau and the heads of various sections have encountered many difficulties. Despite repeated setting of work dates, no one has reported for work. The Baoshan County Party Affairs Reorganization Committee, Public Funds and Public Property Management Office, Education Bureau, Education Association, Census Bureau, Luodian Chamber of Commerce, Transportation Affairs Office, First District Party Headquarters, and the Fifth District Public Office, considering that hasty labor recruitment would inevitably lead to incidents, jointly submitted a petition to the Construction Department, requesting it to consider the special circumstances of the county and approve flexible handling. The petition is recorded below: "We respectfully submit this petition regarding the numerous difficulties in recruiting labor for road construction, detailing the facts, and earnestly requesting that you consider the special circumstances and approve flexible handling to provide relief. The recruitment of labor for road construction is a general matter and should be carried out in accordance with the order. Our county has organized an assistance association to help with the implementation. After repeated detailed discussions, it was unanimously agreed that the county's north-south and east-west roads have been completed in order, and the debt burden for road construction is already substantial, which is not expected to be paid off in a short period. Moreover, based on past experience, the cost of earthwork only accounts for about 6% of the total expenses (including bridges and culverts), while land prices, house and tomb relocation, cinder, bridges, and all other projects are not included. Considering the county's financial resources, land prices cannot be allocated, and the cost of bridges and culverts is even greater. Therefore, immediate action cannot be taken, and the unfinished dirt roads are useless. To complete them, it is estimated that each li requires 2,000 yuan, totaling more than 100,000 yuan. How can we raise funds when the previous debt has not been cleared? Previously, we jointly requested the Baoshan County Government to submit a petition to your department, requesting that the extra mu tax for road construction, which is higher than other counties, be used as a substitute payment to hire workers for construction. However, several months have passed without a reply from your department. Later, we repeatedly received strict orders from former Director Wang to proceed, and the authorities had no choice but to reluctantly comply, separately investigating each household in accordance with the regulations, compiling a register of labor recruitment, and submitting it for the record. Immediately afterward, work start dates were set and efforts were made to urge participation. However, those who advised were sincere, but those who listened were indifferent. Although the staff of the competent authorities and the heads of various sections have been working hard, posting notices and trying to resist, and the good and weak are complying outwardly but resisting passively, no one has reported for work despite repeated setting of work dates. Hasty action will inevitably lead to incidents. The actual effect of road administration will not be achieved, and the hidden dangers of security have been laid, which is not a blessing for the region. In this situation, not only is progress hopeless, but even stagnation is worrying. We respectfully present the crux of the matter to the director in detail: (1) This county is adjacent to Shanghai, and most of the villagers work in Shanghai in addition to farming. Most of the river and road construction is contracted by outsiders, so it is particularly difficult to promote direct labor recruitment. (2) The cost of living in this county is increasing daily. The people are struggling for food and clothing, and even if they are hired, they want to choose jobs with higher wages. If labor is forcibly recruited, no one will respond. (3) The people of this county generally believe that those who have already built roads enjoy the benefits, while those who continue to build roads increase their labor burden. The methods before and after seem unfair. This opinion is particularly prevalent, making it difficult to start labor recruitment. The above three reasons show that the labor recruitment system is difficult to implement suddenly in this county. Reading the late Premier's theory of caring for the people's livelihood, we cannot bear to impose heavy burdens on our people through urgent levies. We have also found that this county has been collecting taxes for road construction since 1921, and now it has been nearly ten years. Many north-south and east-west county roads and township branch roads have been completed, and the convenience of transportation is superior to other counties. For future road construction matters, we should adopt a gradual approach, both for clearing old debts and promoting road administration, which will benefit both the economy and public opinion. If we follow the department's regulations and add multiple lanes to the existing county roads, forcing uniform labor recruitment at the same time, regardless of whether it causes local resentment, the funds for all bridges, culverts, land prices, and cinder have not been raised, and there will be nothing to cope with. The unfinished dirt roads (this county is a water town, and there are a total of 53 large and small bridges on the north-south county roads. If they cannot be planned and carried out at the same time, then what is built will be dirt roads that are disconnected by water) will not be practical. After a while, they will still be overgrown with weeds, wasting the arable land of farmers. We are deeply afraid that the policy of benefiting the people will instead harm them. Our county has built county roads over the years, exhausting local public and private financial resources and enthusiastically participating, which is earlier than other counties. Only because the debt is deep, we should act according to our ability. Therefore, at the last general meeting, two methods were decided: (1) From the annual income collected by the county's transportation office, after repaying the loan and interest, we will consider the economic situation and start construction on Chengyue Road within the five routes that have been submitted, and build the other routes in stages. (2) The county's labor recruitment for road construction plans to use the extra mu tax, which is higher than other counties, as a substitute payment, temporarily using the hiring system and postponing the labor recruitment system. The above two resolutions have been discussed for a long time, and everyone agreed. We dare to present them clearly and earnestly request the director to consider the special circumstances of the region and approve flexible handling. We will be extremely grateful. Respectfully presented to Sun, Director of the Jiangsu Provincial Construction Department."

The Significance of Inspecting Huabian (Lace) Commerce 121

▲ The Ministry of Industry and Commerce Instructs Shanghai Merchant Groups to Explain

The Shanghai National General Chamber of Commerce and the Shanghai Special Municipality Merchant Groups Reorganization Committee jointly received an order from the Ministry of Industry and Commerce: "Regarding the instruction: It has been found that the association previously received a telegram from the Shanghai Special Municipality Lace Embroidery Trade Association Preparatory Committee (hereinafter referred to as the Preparatory Committee) opposing the draft inspection rules for lace inspection proposed by the Shanghai Commodity Inspection Bureau (hereinafter referred to as the Inspection Bureau), claiming that it hinders foreign trade and requesting its abolition. The telegram requested a detailed consideration of the situation. We have ordered the Shanghai Commodity Inspection Bureau to review and reply and have informed you in advance. Now, according to the bureau's reply, the inspection of lace was requested by Shanghai Dafeng Lace Store, Pudong Qinchang Lace Factory, Yantai Zhongxing Factory, Wenzhou Chentongli Store, Wuxi Hengchang Lace Factory, Changshu Yuanshun Company, Xiaoshan Jinglun Factory, Longhua Company, Rugao Dafeng Public Factory, Ningbo Lousantai Factory, Shanghai Dada Company, Pudong Dacheng Factory, Shaoxing Zhenda Lace Net Factory, etc. on November 18 of last year, who signed and stamped their names, detailing the various malpractices in the lace business and requesting inspection to rectify them and promote trade. Therefore, the bureau specifically requested approval from your department to set up a place to prepare for inspection. The merchants did not consider the facts and claimed that the bureau fabricated merchant intentions and deceived your department, which is a deliberate slander. This should be clarified. The lace director, Chen Jinduan, and the deputy director, Tao Yumen, were not acquainted with the director of the bureau. Upon hearing that they were studying art and had expertise, and that they had been engaged in the lace business for many years and had experience, the bureau asked people to obtain their consent and requested their appointment. However, the merchants did not consider the facts and claimed that the bureau placed private individuals, which is also a deliberate slander. This should be clarified. The bureau's income and expenditure, in addition to detailed records in the budget, final accounts, and various books that can be audited, also has a report submitted to your department for verification and distributed to the merchants of various commodities inspected for confirmation. The bureau's finances have long been public and there are no malpractices. The merchants did not consider the facts and claimed that the bureau was seeking private gain, which is also a deliberate slander. This should be clarified. The director of the Shanghai bureau always worried about the estrangement between officials and merchants and sought cooperation between officials and merchants in everything. Therefore, after drafting the lace inspection rules, the bureau sent letters to the merchants in the industry to solicit opinions, hoping to gather wisdom and benefit from each other. However, the merchants did not sincerely discuss the rules with the bureau but declared and opposed them in the newspaper. What is the intention? We do not understand. However, the merchants did not consider the facts and arbitrarily slandered the bureau for fabricating merchant intentions, deceiving your department, employing private individuals to seek private gain, and seem to be responsible for morality and criminal law. Regarding the reasons for the order, in addition to the items in the lace inspection rules pointed out by the merchants, we will sign and present them separately for your review. We should first report the various points pointed out in the merchants' telegram for your review." According to this, the verification is the actual situation. The bureau previously received a request from Shanghai Dafeng Lace Store and more than ten other companies to inspect lace for rectification, and reported it to your department for approval. Later, according to the Preparatory Committee's telegram of opposition, the bureau sent the original submission to your department for verification. It was confirmed that the representatives of the merchants signed and stamped their names, and there was no fraud. The Preparatory Committee's Lin Zhangrong, Li Jiansan, Cheng Wenming, etc. did not consider the facts and falsely claimed that the bureau fabricated merchant intentions, which is inappropriate. As for the inferiority of exported lace goods, the German Bremen Chamber of Commerce's report, forwarded by the embassy in Germany in January of this year, stated that the quality of lace was poor and 40% to 50% had to be rejected, which could not be accepted. This is clear evidence. Moreover, German Yantai companies have used technicians to inspect exported lace. Japan also has places to inspect exported silk fabrics. The Preparatory Committee said that lace embroidery goods are the same as silk fabrics and cannot establish an exchange, which is not a valid argument. As for the inspection rules, the bureau first sent the draft to the merchants in the industry to study in order to seek official-merchant cooperation, originally to solicit opinions and achieve the best results. However, the merchants did not contact the bureau and immediately declared and opposed it in the newspaper, which is even more inappropriate. Considering that the merchants' knowledge is insufficient, we will refrain from further investigation. However, the association is a leading organization in the business community and should correct such publicity based on justice. You should be informed of this order."

The Ministry of Interior Orders Investigation and Repair of Tang Dynasty Pagodas 122

▲ The Pinghu Citizens Living in Shanghai Telegraph to Request Approval

There are twin pagodas built in the Tang Dynasty in Pinghu County, which are earlier than Leifeng and Baochu and are the only ancient sites in western Zhejiang. Recently, someone suddenly planned to dismantle and sell them. Upon learning of this, Pinghu citizens living in Shanghai, Feng Heng and Wu Jing, immediately detailed the situation and telegraphed the Ministry of Interior, requesting it to order the Zhejiang Civil Affairs Department to instruct the Pinghu County Government to repair them immediately to protect the ancient sites and prevent danger. Later, the Ministry of Interior, according to the submission, telegraphed the Zhejiang Civil Affairs Department to investigate and handle the matter, and replied to Feng and others on that day: "The twin pagodas are ancient sites and someone is planning to dismantle and destroy them. Please telegraph the province to instruct the county to repair them." We have ordered the Zhejiang Civil Affairs Department to instruct the county government to handle it. You should be informed."

The Ministry of Communications Broadly Recruits Postal Savings Talents 125

The Postal Savings and Remittance Bureau of the General Directorate of Posts received Instruction No. 1065 from the Ministry of Communications yesterday: "Regarding the order to comply: It has been found that the positions of Deputy Director of the General Directorate of Posts and inspectors of various postal districts are specifically responsible for inspecting postal affairs in various places. Among them, the inspection of funds is extremely important, and most of the funds belong to savings and remittances. Now that the savings and remittance business is expanding vigorously, the supervisory responsibilities of the personnel are heavier than before. In the future, the performance of the Deputy Directors and inspectors who have supervisory responsibilities will be stipulated separately by the two general bureaus, and the two general bureaus will conduct practical assessments to show prudence. All matters such as promotion, advancement, transfer, appointment, acting, and dismissal shall be handled properly by the two bureaus. In addition to distributing this to the subordinate offices, the General Directorate is hereby ordered to comply immediately and notify all subordinate offices accordingly. This order."

Wusong Inspection Bureau Handles Fishing and Salt 126

The fish merchants in Wusong, including Cuisheng, Doufeng, and Shentai, considering that during last year's fishing season, the patrol vessels Junliang and Antao of the Yangtze River Patrol Bureau overstepped their authority at Songkou and Paotai Bay, intercepting the remaining fish and salt from fishing boats, disturbing the fishermen and merchants, causing the fishing boats to dare not come to Song to sell fish, causing huge losses to the fish merchants and greatly affecting customs duties and ship donations, jointly submitted a petition to the Anti-Smuggling Bureau, requesting to clarify the boundaries, abide by the established regulations, and avoid confusion and eliminate disputes. The Songjiang Salt Deputy Envoy's Office received instructions from the Ministry of Finance to transfer the handling of the remaining clean salt to the Wusong Inspection Bureau. The bureau's Public Letter No. 17 is recorded below: "Dear Sirs, According to the Songjiang Salt Transportation Deputy Envoy's Office's Instruction No. 130 of April 16th of this year, 'Regarding the notification, according to the Ministry of Finance's instructions, the Deputy Envoy submitted a document to report the situation of handling the remaining clean salt from fishing boats entering the port during the fishing season in the past, requesting the Yangtze River Patrol Bureau not to handle matters in violation of regulations during this fishing season, in order to maintain tax revenue. It has been learned from the instructions. The case of the Yangtze River Patrol Bureau intercepting and extracting fishing salt was previously submitted by the Anti-Smuggling Office. According to the report of Lu Chongdan, Director of the Anti-Smuggling Bureau of the Five Prefectures of Jiangsu, the fishing season is approaching, and he earnestly requests that the Yangtze River Patrol Bureau not intercept fishing salt in violation of regulations, causing disputes. The General Inspection Office was ordered to instruct the Yangtze River Patrol Bureau to comply with the regulations. You are hereby instructed to notify. This order.' Also, the instructions from the Salt Affairs Administration state, 'It has been learned from the presentation that since the direct submission has been made, you should wait for the Ministry of Finance to verify and comply. This order.' Having received these instructions, this bureau and various fish merchants have previously submitted reports. This office has submitted reports to the relevant authorities and instructed compliance. Having received the previous instructions, the director of this bureau is hereby ordered to immediately notify various fish merchants to be informed. This order.' Having received this, we hereby send you a letter and hope that your firm will check it. Sincerely, Shi Jitong, Director of the Bureau."

Measures to Prevent Rabies 127

▲ Register Domestic Dogs and Capture Stray Dogs

The Shanghai County Government recently received an instruction from the Jiangsu Civil Affairs Department, which was forwarded from the Ministry of Health, stating that rabies, also known as hydrophobia, is a type of infectious disease. The cause is the contact of rabies saliva with human skin. People's intelligence is not developed, and they do not pay attention to it. Prevention should be strictly enforced. Now, the Ministry has drafted rules for the registration of domestic dogs and measures for capturing stray dogs, ordering obedience from subordinates. After receiving the order, County Magistrate Leng has instructed the County Public Security Bureau to forward the order to various branches to comply with it strictly and notify the people in advance to avoid misunderstandings.

Two Automobiles Collide, One Dead, Four Injured 131

▲ Moving Truck Collides with Another Vehicle

▲ Sixty-Six-Year-Old Man Dies Instantly

▲ Pianist from New World Garden and Four Others

▲ Also Severely Injured in the Crash

Yesterday evening around 5:30 PM, a moving truck and another automobile collided in front of the New World Company on Nanjing Road. At that time, Jiang Nianbo, a Jiangbei native, aged 66, was injured in a vital spot and died on the spot. At the same time, four people were injured in the crash: (1) A rickshaw puller, injured in the face; (2) Cai Shousheng, a Tianjin native, suffered a head injury, and the injury was not light; (3) Cai's wife, A Bao, aged 21, injured in the face; (4) Cai's apprentice, Zhu Peiyuan, aged 16, suffered skin injuries and bled profusely. Afterwards, Western Constable No. 309 and Chinese Constable No. 604 arrived and sent the deceased's body and the four injured people to Renji Hospital. The car that caused the accident was escorted to the police station for investigation. After the incident, reporters learned that Cai Shousheng was a pianist at the New World Company's rooftop garden, living above the Hongfu Barber Shop in Xiexing Lane, Northern Mud City Bridge. He had just left home with his wife and apprentice to perform at the company when he suddenly encountered this unexpected disaster. It is said that bad luck never comes alone. Recently, incidents of car accidents have been heard every day. However, the death of one and the injury of four in this accident is particularly rare. It is hoped that the police authorities will pay close attention to it.

Trouble in the Sea of Jealousy 132

▲ Xie Liben Fails to Marry

▲ Mu Shijiang Incites a Crowd to Assault

Wei Sheng, currently residing in a thatched cottage in Tanjia Ferry, north of Caojiadu, Shanghai West. He has an uncle named Xie Haijun, who is also twenty-nine years old and works at the Xinsheng Company in Tanjia Ferry. The uncle and nephew often visit each other. Liben has been in Shanghai for many years and is usually quite frugal, so he has saved a little money. Because he is lonely and drifting, he intends to marry and start a family. At the beginning of last month, a friend acted as matchmaker and arranged for Liben to marry a woman surnamed Chen, who lives near his residence and is from the same hometown. Liben's desire for a wife is like waiting for clouds in a severe drought. Not long after the arrangement was made, he started preparing to choose a date for the wedding. Unexpectedly, the woman is only 29 years old and has a beautiful appearance, and many people covet her. Recently, Mu Shijiang, an Anhui native who runs a "tiger stove" (a type of stove for boiling water) at No. 21 Chongxin Workshop in Tanjia Ferry, developed an ambiguous relationship with the woman due to covetousness, and the temperature of their relationship reached a boiling point. Now, suddenly learning that the woman has been betrothed to Xie and will soon be married, it became a love triangle. A storm arose in the sea of jealousy, and Mu developed a determination to harm Xie so that he could seize the woman for himself. Xie invited two burly men, one holding a sharp single-edged sword, one holding a large firewood knife, and one holding a large iron rod. The three of them went to Xie's place. Without asking questions, they surrounded Xie Liben and attacked him with knives and sticks, engaging in a bloody battle. Xie immediately fell to the ground after being stabbed, covered in blood and flesh, and unconscious. Seeing that their purpose had been achieved, the two burly men fled with their knives and sticks. Patrol Chief Hu Lizhong of the 6th District Police Station on Guangfu Road and Extra Patrol Chief Wu of the Shenghe Long Oil Factory rushed to the scene after learning of the incident. Unexpectedly, the assailant Mu Shijiang stepped forward and confessed, "I was the one who harmed Xie, and I am fully responsible," etc. Seeing that the injured person was on the verge of death, Patrol Chief Hu and others immediately arrested him and took him back to the 6th District Police Station, and the injured person was taken by car to the Red Cross Hospital on Haig Road for treatment. According to the doctor's examination, Xie Liben had two knife wounds on his head, two on his left upper arm, and the wounds were very deep with profuse bleeding. Four fingers of his left hand were cut off, leaving only the thumb, and half of the back of his hand was cut off. He also suffered one knife wound each on the left and right sides, for a total of seven knife wounds. His breath was weak, and his condition was very dangerous, and his life was feared. Xie Haijun, Liben's uncle, then filed a case, requesting a thorough investigation. After separate interrogations by the District Chief Duan, Xie Haijun, the plaintiff, stated, "I am 29 years old, from Anhui, and currently work at Xinsheng Company. Today, my nephew Liben was slashed by Mu. I don't know the reason. However, my nephew's injuries are dangerous, so please punish him severely," etc. The assailant Mu Shijiang stated, "I am 20 years old, from Anhui, and currently run a 'tiger stove' at No. 21 Chongxin Workshop. I harmed Xie because I had a grudge against him," etc. After obtaining the confessions, District Chief Duan ordered the assailant to be temporarily detained and sent to the court today to be dealt with according to the law.

French Police Raid an Organization Specializing in Trafficking Women and Children 134

The Shanghai Times reported that the French Concession police raided an organization specializing in trafficking women and children on Ningxing Street yesterday morning (the 19th), arresting two bandits and rescuing four young women. According to their confession, the gang has organizations all over China and mostly lures women from the northern and central provinces to Shanghai, then transfers them to Xiamen, Guangzhou, and Nanjing to be sold as prostitutes or maids. Their methods of luring are mostly to entice ignorant and uneducated young women with words about how high wages are and how comfortable life is in Shanghai and other places. Once they fall into the trap, it is difficult to escape. Most of these women are textile workers, and their parents are mostly poor and unable to conduct large-scale investigations, so few cases have been solved. Recently, the number of reports of missing young women in the French Concession has suddenly increased, and the police have stepped up their investigation, leading to the raid. When the detectives entered the house, the four women were all hiding in a corner of a room upstairs. At first, when they saw many people, they suspected that they were being taken to a southern port and were extremely panicked. When they were told that they were police officers who had come to rescue them and take them home, they were overjoyed beyond description. It is now known that the organization that was raided is the gang's headquarters in Shanghai, used exclusively for confining deceived young women awaiting transfer.

Record of the Trial of the Kidnapping Case of the Young Master of the Tongshunxing Machine Factory 135

▲ Ten Irrelevant People Released

▲ The Remaining Twelve People Remanded in Custody

Xia Sheng, the son of Wang Shunjin, the owner of the Tongshunxing Machine Factory at No. 533 Gongping Road, was kidnapped by bandits on the night of the 25th of last month and hidden at No. 644 Xinzha Road. Later, he was rescued by detectives from the Huishan Police Station, who also apprehended fourteen male and female criminals for interrogation. This was previously reported. The police station learned that Wang Maoyi, Wang Yudong, Liu Guilin, Shao Hongqing, Chi Futian, Zhang Jinfa, Xia Zisheng, Wang Ren, and other eleven male and female suspects arrested by the 3rd Branch of the 5th District of Zhabei were also accomplices in the case. They were specially taken back to the police station, and it was also found that these people had also committed robberies of Li Arong at No. 50 McKinley Road and of a certain nunnery on Huishan Road. The fourteen people previously arrested, except for Zhou Shen, who had died of smallpox, and the eleven people brought from Zhabei, were all sent to the Special District Local Court the day before yesterday, where Judge Feng interrogated them. The police lawyer stated that Yang Sihu, Chen Lidian, Ji Sha, Sun Chenghuai, Wang Maozheng, Shao Huasheng, Yin Kaifa, Sun Jitai, and the women Sun Yuan and Jia Jiang, etc., had no evidence of committing a crime and requested that the charges be withdrawn. Judge Feng approved the request and ordered the ten men and women to be released first. The police lawyer continued, "There are still two defendants, Wang Laowu and Wang Jiajiu, who committed a kidnapping case in the Chinese territory. The kidnapped person was surnamed Chen, and the local police station sent detectives to the case and requested their transfer." After Judge Feng reviewed the official documents, he ordered the two Wangs to be handed over to the detectives of the 3rd Branch of the 5th District to be taken back for interrogation. Therefore, only twelve male and female defendants, including Jia Kuizhi, remained. Wang Shunjin then described the kidnapping of his son, saying that five bandits broke into his house on the night of March 25. Three bandits held pistols and first demanded the keys, opened the box, and robbed him of more than one hundred yuan in silver, as well as a gold ring and a gold watch. Then they snatched his three-year-old son and subsequently sent five letters demanding a ransom of two thousand yuan, as well as a dozen gold rings and gold watches. Because he had no funds, he ignored them. Wang also identified Li Zhaozhen as one of the defendants, saying that he was at the scene at the time, but he could not identify the others. Gu Fulian, Wang's relative, testified that Xia Sheng was in his arms at the time when he was snatched away by the second bandit who broke in. He could not recognize the bandit's face because he was frightened. When questioned, Jia Kuizhi, Li Zhaozhen, Zhou Guanqing, Wang Maoyi, Zhang Yudong, and Liu Guilin all admitted to kidnapping the child and said that Jia Da, who was at large, was the mastermind. The remaining Chen Lilan, Shao Hongqing, Chi Futian, Zhang Jinfa, Xia Zisheng, and Wang Ren all denied the charges and hired lawyer Fan Gang to defend them. Judge Feng ordered the twelve people to be detained separately and adjourned the hearing to a later date.

White Pills Beside a Woman Trafficking on the Xiamen Steamer 138

▲ Possibly Drugs to Lure Children

▲ Two Trafficked Boys and Girls Rescued

Yesterday morning around 6:00 AM, Chen Shaoting, an investigator from the Society for the Relief of Women and Children, boarded the Taikoo Company's Xiamen steamer Zhejiang as it was about to set sail to investigate whether there were any traffickers luring women and children for export. He found a woman, about forty years old, in the cabin with a boy and a girl, and her behavior was suspicious. He questioned her, and the woman stated that her name was Ding Dai, 48 years old, from Quanzhou, Xiamen. She claimed that the boy she was carrying was purchased in Shanghai for 44 silver dollars, and the girl was purchased for 136 silver dollars, and that she did not lure them. When questioned, the boy stated that his name was Cai Bao, 7 years old, and he did not know anything else. The girl stated that her name was Zhang Asan, 14 years old, from Songjiang. The police then found two small white pills, similar in shape to camphor pills, beside the woman. The woman claimed that they were round candies that children liked to eat. However, the police chief did not believe her and carefully examined the two round pills. They did not appear to be made of sugar. Whether they were drugs to lure children needed to be determined by a doctor. They were all ordered to be sent to the Local Court for disposal.

Woman Appeals for Divorce 141

▲ Expresses Dissatisfaction with the Abduction of the Bride

▲ Attempt to Reconcile Fails

Zhang Ruie, a young woman from Tongzhou, residing at No. 6 Wangjiazhai, Gaolang Bridge, is currently a female worker in a textile factory. In the past, her father, Zhang Jiushou, arranged her marriage to Shen Jinshan, the son of Shen Maolian, from the same hometown. Because of the abduction of the bride that occurred in the Qianzhai residence, Zhang Ruie is very dissatisfied and has hired lawyer Yin Shengwu to file a lawsuit in the Shanghai Local Court, requesting the dissolution of the marriage contract. Yesterday, Judge Yang Keqian opened the court to interrogate the case. The plaintiff, Zhang Ruie, stated, "I am 16 years old, from Tongzhou. (Question) Who is Shen Jinshan to you? (Answer) I didn't know anything about him until they came to abduct me, and then I understood. Shen Jinshan is my father's betrothed fiancé, but I don't want to, so I filed a lawsuit," etc. The judge said, "You are only sixteen years old this year, which is not legal. You must have a legal representative. Your father is your guardian. Are you willing or not?" (Answer) "I don't want to. You said that my two brothers are robbers, but I am young and don't understand the reasons, so please take care of me." (Question) "When was the bride abducted?" (Answer) "It was on the first day of the third lunar month this year. I escaped back on the same day." The defendant, Shen Jinshan, stated, "I am 20 years old, from Tongzhou, living at No. 18, 21 Jian Tou, Gaolang Bridge, and I make a living by working. (Question) If she doesn't want to marry you, what can you do? (Answer) I must have her, but I did not abduct the bride. Because her father and daughter had an argument at home that day, my sister-in-law went to mediate. Unexpectedly, her father, Zhang Jiushou, called thirty or forty people from the Tilam Bridge area and snatched her back. (Question) If you say you did not abduct the bride, why did so many people snatch her back?" The defendant was speechless. "How much betrothal gift did you give?" (Answer) "Seventy yuan, arranged by Tang Lide as the matchmaker," etc. The judge ordered Zhang Jiushou, a related person, to come to court to testify, "I am 47 years old. My daughter Ruie was betrothed to the defendant when she was eleven years old, and the betrothal gift was only thirty yuan. (Question) What are your intentions now? (Answer) I have to ask my daughter. (Question) Was the bride abducted? (Answer) Yes, she was abducted," etc. Shen Maolian, a related person, stated, "I am 53 years old, also from Tongzhou. The defendant, Shen Jinshan, is my son." The rest of his statement was the same as the defendant's. The judge attempted to reconcile the two parties in court, but both parties refused to comply. Therefore, he invited Prosecutor Zhu to the court to express his opinion, which was roughly that the plaintiff's request was without sufficient reason and should be rejected. The judge then announced that the debate was over and that the verdict would be announced on the 21st of this month, and then adjourned the court.

Little Sister Wishes to Follow Old Husband 142

▲ Unwilling for Family to Interfere

▲ Files Lawsuit to Prevent

Yuan Ziyin from Funing, Jiangbei, age 34, and Xu Xiaomei (i.e., Gu Xu’s, age 18), a woman from Yancheng, have fallen in love and are cohabitating at the third house in Xinglong Lane, Gaolang Bridge. However, the woman's mother, Xu You’s, is vehemently opposed because the daughter had already been betrothed to Xu Xiaosi. Therefore, she has repeatedly intervened, intending to take Xiaomei back. Unexpectedly, Xiaomei wishes to spend her days with Gu Ziyin, who is older. Xu Xiaomei and Gu Ziyin have jointly retained lawyer Song Shixiang and filed a petition with the Shanghai District Court requesting a judgment ordering the defendant (i.e., Xu You’s) and others not to interfere. The petition states roughly that in November of the 17th year of the Republic [1928], matchmaker Yang Shousong arranged for Xiaomei to be betrothed to Ziyin, and 80 yuan in silver was given as bride price. It was originally intended to hold the wedding last autumn, but Xu You's excessive demands led to the postponement of the wedding date. Fortunately, Xiaomei, understanding the greater good, came to Ziyin's home this spring and hastily married. What's done is done, so they request that their union be fulfilled and that the defendants be ordered not to interfere. Yesterday morning, Judge Yang Keqian opened the court for trial. Gu Ziyin testified that he is 34 years old and makes a modest living. (Asked) Have you married Xiaomei? (Answered) I have married her. I got engaged to Xiaomei on the 24th day of the 11th month of the year before last. At that time, I sent 80 yuan in silver as bride price, as well as four packages of fruit and other gifts. Because my mother-in-law Xu You’s demanded an additional 200 yuan in bride price, I was unable to raise the money in time, so I missed the wedding date. On the fourth day of the second month of this year, Xiaomei ran to my house, and we hastily married that evening. Gu Xu’s (i.e., Xiaomei) testified that she is 18 years old. She was betrothed to Gu Ziyin the year before last. Later, because her mother demanded an excessive bride price, the Gu family was unable to marry her. Unexpectedly, on the third day of the first month of this year, her mother and elder brother summoned an old woman to their home to assess her character, intending for her to become someone's concubine. Hearing this, she refused and, out of desperation, left on the afternoon of the third day of the second month to meet with Gu Ziyin. They spent the night in a hotel, and the next day (i.e., the fourth day) they found a house and began cohabitating with Gu. On the night of entering the house, they lit candles and burned incense together in the pavilion room upstairs, bowing to Heaven and Earth, thus consummating their marriage. As for the husband's age, although he is older, he is very honest and not like those slick and oily types, so she is very satisfied. Moreover, this marriage was arranged by her mother, and so on. The defendant Xu You’s testified that Xiaomei is her daughter, and she does not know Gu Ziyin, so how could she have betrothed her to him? Her daughter Xiaomei was betrothed to Xu Xiaosi as a wife on the sixth day of the eleventh month of last year by matchmakers Shousong, You Fubi, and Zhu Zhaoqing. (Asked) Why were there three matchmakers? (Answered) This is our hometown custom, to have three matchmakers and six witnesses. Now Xu Xiaosi works as a baker in a flatbread shop in Nanmen, Wuxi. When the engagement was set, three tables of wine were prepared, and the Xu family sent 24 yuan in silver, along with a gold bracelet and two gold rings. When the Xu family demands the person, how will she deal with it? Please investigate. Witness Yang Shousong testified that he is 65 years old, from Yancheng. The defendant is his wife's younger sister. He works as a road laborer and has never been a matchmaker. His sister-in-law Xiaomei was betrothed to Xu Xiaosi by You Xiaosan, Zhu Zhaoqing, and Yang You’s. On the day of the engagement, the woman's family prepared one table of wine, and so on. The judge, having heard the testimonies, ordered both parties to go outside and reconcile, and also instructed that the court still needed to investigate the truth in order to make a ruling. Thereupon, the court was adjourned.

This is truly a novel twist in debt collection.

Ji Guangui was sentenced to one month in prison, Zhang Yingming was fined eighty yuan, and the opium paraphernalia was confiscated.

▲ Resulting in Loss of Life

Page 16

In the first month of the lunar year, she suddenly took poison.

After deliberation, the judge instructed for further investigation. Sandboat Runs Aground and Is Robbed 155

The Hongdafu, a sandboat from Laiyang, Shandong, was leased from the Shandong Renfeng Company in February for a term of two years, with a contract stipulating that all repairs during the lease period would be the responsibility of the lessee, the Gongji Company. This was its third trip from Shanghai to Laiyang, carrying goods such as native cloth and yarn remnants. The boat sailed to Qingkou when a hurricane erupted on the sea, and the rudder was broken by the waves, rendering it unable to steer. It drifted with the wind and waves for a day and a night before running aground near Dalian. The bow of the ship was damaged, and eight crew members were thrown overboard when it ran aground. The ship sounded the gong for help, but no ships passed by. It was spotted by pirates, who boarded the ship and robbed it, taking all the cotton yarn and other goods. They also shot and wounded the shipowner, surnamed Yang. Fortunately, a Japanese coal ship passed by and saw the situation, sending the ship's crew to Dalian. The ship remained aground on the beach. Yesterday, four members of the crew arrived in Shanghai by boat to report to the company. It is said that the ship was carrying goods worth 40,000 yuan. Whether the ship can be repaired will depend on whether it can be towed out of danger and the condition of the hull can be inspected.

Request for Assistance in Reporting Illegal Construction 156

The Shanghai Special Municipality Public Security Bureau received a letter yesterday from the Bureau of Public Works stating that the construction and repair of public and private buildings in the city should, according to regulations, be reported to this Bureau before work begins, so that this Bureau can issue construction or repair miscellaneous licenses to ensure compliance. This Bureau will spare no effort to crack down on any unauthorized construction, projects exceeding the scope of the license, or projects that do not conform to the reported plans and are intended to deceive. However, the city is vast and the projects are complex, making it difficult for the Bureau's inspection personnel to be comprehensive. If any of your district offices encounter any of the above-mentioned illegal situations that have not been detected by this Bureau, it is hoped that you will provide assistance and report the illegal situation to your Bureau at any time, which will then be forwarded to this Bureau for verification. In cases where the situation is urgent and requires immediate action, district offices may directly notify the competent department of this Bureau (i.e., the Fourth Department) by telephone to coordinate the handling. Before notifying this Bureau, it is especially hoped that the district offices will not directly impose penalties or revoke the licenses they have issued in order to avoid ambiguity. It is requested that you investigate and inform all subordinates to comply accordingly.

Incoming Document

Labor Statistics Work and Plans (Continued) 163

▲ Shanghai Special Municipality Social Affairs Bureau

(I) (J) Labor agreements and labor agreement statistics have only developed in recent years. In 1926, the International Labour Office convened labor statistics experts from various countries for the Third Conference to discuss compilation methods, striving for international uniformity to facilitate comparison. Labor agreement statistics are used to study the employment conditions and work systems of groups, with the aim of standardizing employment conditions, eliminating labor-management disputes and monopolies, and balancing the negotiating power of both labor and management. The unit of statistics is a labor agreement, and its main items include the nature of the contracting parties, the scope of application, the agreed items, events, validity period, arbitration method, business classification, the number of related factories, and the number of workers. The number of agreements in effect at the beginning of the year, the number of renewed agreements, the number of terminated agreements, and the number of agreements in effect at the end of the year. As for the provisions in the agreement regarding wages, working hours, and individual employment conditions, they should be separately classified into wage statistics, etc. (K) Strikes and lockouts. A strike is when workers, in order to demand conditions or express opinions, combine as a group and temporarily stop working in order to promote the recognition or awareness of the other party. A lockout is when the management, in order to demand conditions, temporarily closes factories in order to promote the recognition or awareness of the other party. According to the results of the International Labour Statistics Experts Conference, strikes and lockouts can be combined into one category called labor disputes. Labor disputes can be said to be a serious manifestation of conflicts between labor and management, and the social loss is great. If we want to study and resolve camp-based disputes, we naturally need to start with compiling statistics. The important items that should be studied in the statistics include the number of strikes and lockouts, the industry, the nationality of the management, cause analysis, result analysis, mediation methods, the number of related factories, the number of labor participants, the number of extended days, the number of working days lost, and the amount of wages lost. Go-slows are considered strikes in the laws of various countries and are also included in this type of statistics. (L) Labor disputes. Any labor-management conflict in which labor and management are negotiating and one party continues to work is called a labor dispute. In terms of the degree of conflict, strikes and lockouts are of course the most serious, but in terms of the number of cases that occur, then disputes should be promoted. Disputes can be said to be the initial stage of disputes. If disputes are not resolved properly, they will lead to strikes and lockouts. However, if disputes do not reach the level of strikes and lockouts, society will not pay much attention to this, and it is not easy to investigate. Therefore, very few countries compile this type of statistics, unless the collection of materials is particularly convenient. However, during labor disputes, it cannot be said that there is no considerable loss in terms of material costs and mental stress, and disputes are the fuse for disputes. Therefore, in order to show where the crux of labor disputes lies and to prevent problems before they occur, if there is not much difficulty in collecting materials, it is best to compile statistics. The content is the same as labor strikes and lockouts. The scope of labor statistics, of course, is not limited to the above-mentioned items, but the most important statistics are roughly like this. However, it must be known that the field of labor statistics expands with the degree of industrialization and the development of labor undertakings. For example, when labor was not developed in the past, there were naturally no statistics on labor agreements, etc. Therefore, to what extent will labor problems expand in the future, and the field of labor statistics will also develop to that extent. It seems that there is no need to study this here.

▲ Past Work Since the winter of 1927, this bureau has begun to conduct labor statistics, with the aim of observing and planning to solve the city's labor problems through statistical exploration. At the beginning of the project, everything was in the planning stage. From January 1928, three types of statistics, namely wage index, strike statistics, and labor dispute statistics, were first implemented on a trial basis to meet the urgent needs of administrative reference. In the spring of 1929, three books, "Trial Compilation of Wage Index of Shanghai Special Municipality", "Strike Statistics Report of Shanghai Special Municipality", and "Labor Dispute Statistics Report of Shanghai Special Municipality", were published and distributed by Shanghai Datong Bookstore on Fuzhou Road. The process and results of each statistic are detailed in a special booklet, so there is no need to talk about it here. At the same time, we are also engaged in compiling a series of labor statistics books to introduce labor statistics knowledge, hoping that various places can gradually organize them. The list of books that have been published and are in printing is as follows: Compilation Method of Cost of Living Index (Published by Shanghai Commercial Press) Unemployment Statistics Method (ibid.) Compilation Method of Industrial Labor Dispute Statistics (ibid.) Worker Accident Statistics Method (In printing) Overview of the American Housing Problem (ibid.) Household Livelihood Survey Method (ibid.) Labor Agreement Statistics Method (ibid.) In the second half of 1928, statistical personnel were added, and it was planned to conduct surveys on the living standards of Shanghai workers, cost of living index, retail price survey, and unemployment statistics. Among them, unemployment statistics are of a experimental nature. It was held in September and took three months to complete the survey. The results have been published in the eighth issue of the Bureau's Social Monthly, which is also published by Shanghai Datong Bookstore. In 1929, the statistics on wages, strikes, lockouts, and labor disputes were continued, and the survey on the cost of living of workers' families and the retail price survey were started. The cost of living survey adopts the standard sampling method, selecting 400 workers' families for investigation, with a period of one year. Staff are sent to each family every day to replace or guide bookkeeping, with each person managing about 20 families. Strict inspection is carried out every month and calculated at any time. By March 1930, the investigation part can be completely concluded. After that, it is just the work of calculation and compilation. The retail price survey has been conducted by the bureau since January 1929. In addition to the market prices of meat and vegetable dishes, the survey is conducted once a week. Rice and grain are surveyed three times a month, and the rest of the items are surveyed once a month. The goods surveyed are as detailed as possible, and most of them are based on the results of the cost of living survey and are consumed daily by workers. In addition to the small vegetable markets, more than 150 merchants were surveyed in the city. The customers of these retail stores are mostly workers. In the autumn of 1928, because we had fully obtained the belief and understanding of the above-mentioned retail stores, we planned to track down the retail prices from 1926 to the present. Since the beginning of the process, the results have been satisfactory and will be completed soon. The results will be published at the same time as the cost of living index in the future. In addition, the wage survey that we started in 1928 is the actual income of workers, and it is surveyed once a month. First, it is divided according to industry, and then according to male, female, and child workers. In order to understand the detailed wage rate situation in each industry, we planned a wage rate survey from June 1929 and completed the survey in November. The compilation method is to first divide according to industry, and then according to occupation and male, female, and child workers. We are currently in the process of dividing occupations and calculating, and hope to be able to compile and publish it in May 1930. (To be continued)
