Words of Wisdom 164

— Wang Shouyang

▲ When you see beauty, you should look at it like watching clouds and smoke, which disappear in the blink of an eye. You must not be like a photographer who leaves an impression on the ground glass.

▲ Young friends, the heart of believing in a lover is more dedicated than the heart of believing in a career.

▲ Suffering and happiness are closely related. If you don't seek happiness, you will never suffer.

▲ People's conscience is like a bright mirror that can distinguish huge and subtle objects. If it is obscured by evil thoughts, it cannot shine brightly again.

▲ Divorce is an extremely painful thing. Some people enjoy it, and some people are proud of it.

▲ The basis of happiness in life lies in one's own personality and spirit. If the personality falls and the spirit is lost, one will never be able to achieve the goal of happiness.

▲ Love must be close to infatuation to be true love. A little intelligence cannot be added to the word love. It must be completely infatuated to be completely in love.

▲ When something comes, at first you are ashamed and unwilling to do it. As you gradually become tempted by profit, you ignore everything and do it resolutely. Then pain and misfortune will come at any time.

▲ The great French writer Hugo said, "Facts are like clouds, often obscuring people with shadows. Truth is like a star, able to illuminate people with light." However, people know the value of light, but no one cares about truth.

▲ If a person loses his reputation, he must never boast again. Boasting is even more sufficient to publicize sin.

Talking About Hail 165

— Yan Qian

A few days ago, a guest came from Shanghai and said that he encountered hail in the boat, and told me about the shape of the hail, saying that the volume was different, and it was divided into three types. The larger ones were like chicken eggs, the second ones were like walnuts, and the smallest ones were like lotus seeds. Some were split in half, like the bottom of a radish. The spiral pattern on the top was very obvious, with five, six, or seven turns. Two or three turns were transparent. In the middle, there was a center, and among the large and small ones, there were different points, or they were round and complete, or they were extremely incomplete, like flaws. It was suspected that several hailstones merged to form this shape. Because of this guest's words, it caused a debate among the people in the same seat. I thought that empty talk was useless, so it was better to turn the book. So we found the following items together.

Ciyuan: "Hail is rain ice. When there is thunder and rain, the clouds are shocked by electricity and enter the ice and snow line boundary in the high sky, condensing into ice points and snowflakes, and then rotating and uniting to form ice blocks, which fall together with rain." According to this statement, the guest's words are reliable. The spiral pattern with five, six, or seven turns also. The two turns are transparent also. Is it not enough to prove that the theory of ice point snowflakes rotating and uniting is scientific? And the theory that several hailstones merge to form one is also somewhat similar.

Da Dai Li Zhu says: "Yang energy is in the rain, and it is warm like the sun. Yin energy is thin and does not enter, and it fights and becomes hail. Therefore, the Chunqiu Guliang Zhuan says: Hail is a symbol of yin threatening yang." Pi Ya says: "Yin wraps yang to become hail." Li Yueling Zhu says: "Yang is like rain, and yin rises to threaten it, condensing into hail. Liu Xiang said: "When the sun is strong, the rainwater is warm and hot, and the yin energy threatens it and does not enter, then it turns into hail. Therefore, boiling soup is in a closed container, and when it is soaked in sweet spring, it becomes ice. This is its test." The above four statements are the same in meaning as the previous one, but the words and phrases used in ancient and modern times are very different.

However, there is a mysterious saying in Zuo Zhuan: "There is no hail when the sage is on the throne. Even if there is, it is not a disaster." Fortunately, the blind teacher is talking about the origin of hail, not the cause of hail formation. It does not seem to hinder the previous few statements from competing for a place. We should just treat him as nonsense.

In addition, there are other names that must be known, and the stories that run through the other names must also be understood. Yunhui Bu says: "The hail in Tao and Min is called white rain, also called hard head rain." In the seventeenth year of Shaoxing in the Song Dynasty, it rained hail in Lin'an, and the roof tiles of the Taixue were broken. The Xuegong tabooed hail, so they said hard rain. This hard rain can be greatly studied. It is probably always because of believing in nonsense. It is not that the Xuegong is illuminated by the aura of the Supreme Sage and First Teacher and avoids it, but it is because he is afraid of advocating peace talks and falsely accusing Yue Fei. There is no doubt that he is Qin Hui, the prime minister who paid tribute to the Jin Dynasty and called himself a minister.

As for Liu Xiang's boiling soup in a closed container and soaking it in sweet spring to become ice, it is quite similar to the current ice-making and freezing. Or was the ice-making and freezing already invented in China at that time? A smile.

Two Miracles in Taixing 166

— Zhang Yan

▲ Wen Tianxiang Zi Taixing has a simple and honest folk customs, so the people are polite. And the Confucian Temple in the city is very spacious. The structure is also exquisite. Solemn and magnificent. Golden and resplendent. The four screen doors in front of the Minglun Hall are made of Phoebe zhennan. The door is carved with an absolutely large Kui character. (Made in the style of Hejin) More than one foot square. The brushwork is vigorous. Exceptionally delicate. It was written by Wen Tianxiang. According to legend, when Wenshan was writing the ghost character, his wrist strength gradually became insufficient. He kicked with his left foot and used his right wrist to borrow the strength of his foot, so he went up smoothly. Therefore, the ghost character sentence is more vigorous. Although it has been thousands of years, it is still intact and undamaged. It is really a Mo Bao.

▲ Wu Mu's hand-planted flower is forty miles away from Taixing. The town has a Yue Wang Temple. It covers a large area. It is the best place for pavilions, terraces, flowers and trees. There is a magnolia tree in the courtyard. Three people embrace it. It is only one foot high. And the branches and leaves cover an area of one mu. It does not wither in the severe winter. It was planted by Wu Mu himself in the past. It is protected by carved railings. Emerald green and lush. Outside the temple, there are iron-cast statues of Qin Hui and his wife. When the merchants and residents of the town have bad business, they often like to go to Qin Hui's wife, Wang, and stroke her breasts with both hands to ensure that business will be booming the next day. The language is very absurd. The matter is also tasteless. However, it can also be seen that Wu Mu's loyalty is deeply moving.

Talking About Drunkenness 167

— Ruoqi

The play "Drunkenness" is a play that is often practiced by those who know how to sing Huashan. However, the movements are heavy, and the singing is all in Siping tune. It is not easy to excel without a high and low voice. There are even fewer amateur performers who practice this play. I am very fond of Hu Su, and I especially like to play "Guifei Drunk". Two years ago, I hired a teacher to learn this play. A month later, I barely succeeded. Every time I want to practice, there are very few people who are in tune with me, so I can't satisfy my desire to play the piano. Recently, the Beikai and Dachina phonograph companies have two new records of "Drunkenness". I quickly bought them and listened to them. I can learn the tune and play the piano at the same time. My wish has been fulfilled. What could be happier? Now I will describe the highlights of the two records separately.

▲ Xun Huisheng's record has a long Ah character tune at the beginning of the Daoban Huilong. This record cuts it off probably because of the length. The sentence "Hede Nu Zhuanjingjing" is sung in Yuanban. The last Jing character is composed of the Gongpu Liuliu Chisan characters. The Liu character is on the board, and the Chi character is on the eye. These three characters seem ordinary, but they are very pleasant to hear on the strings. The sentence "Niangniang Youhua Lai Wenni" has the Pu Sishang Fan Chi Shang Gong Chi Shang Wu Shang Wu Liu Fan Liu Wu Shang Liu slowly and lowly sung. It is intoxicating to hear.

▲ Jiang Junjia's record. The two records that Junjia recorded have complete lyrics from beginning to end. There is also the Ah character tune. However, it is also a fast three-beat. The opera Gao Pei Erzhe is slightly different from what Huisheng sang. Huisheng wins with gentleness, charm, and sweetness, while this wins with clarity, vigor, and fluency. Each has its own advantages. The three characters "Leng Qing Qing" in the ending of "Qu Ye" are high and inexhaustible, which shows his skill. After listening to it, I still seem to have a lingering taste, left between my teeth and lips.

Anecdotes of Yang Liaogong 168

— Wang Yanjin

During the Qing Dynasty, when Yang Liaogong was the Guangwen of Baoshan, he had a teacher-student relationship with my father. However, he ignored the formalities. When he took office, he did not bring servants. He had poet friends Shen Long and Wang Chi, who followed the school. It was originally a cold yamen. He often visited with my father. His colleagues or people in the county often invited him to banquets, but he refused. Every day, he went to the western suburbs of the city to visit and play. When it was time for lunch, he wanted to stay for a meal. Gong said that there was no need for dishes. He only needed ten eggs, half a catty of white sugar, a bowl of boiled water, and a pot of Longjing tea. When my father went to the school, he entertained him with a can of braised beef, ten pancakes, and half a catty of Wen wine. My father Dong took charge of the Western School. He opened a room in the western corner of the school and named it Qu Xuan. He asked Gong to write. After Gong wrote the plaque, he also wrote a record for it. The record said: "Prince built a room in the west of the Western School of the city. It is titled Qu Xuan. Some say, this is not Qu's Xuan. Why is it called Qu Xuan? I say, what is Qu's to have and what is not Qu's to have in all things in the world? Why be so narrow-minded between Qu's to have and not Qu's to have? Moreover, in the west of this room, there are lotus ditches in summer and lotus ditches in autumn. Why can't any of them be Xuanqu? What does Qu Xuan have to do with Qu? Who is Qu Xuan to Qu?" After saying that, some people called it Xuanqu. I then used Xuanqu. Yang Liaogong wrote. This record was hung in the room for many years. The reporter still saw and remembered it when he studied at the school. Unexpectedly, the headmaster of the school was a non-person. The tables and chairs were almost destroyed. It is not known where the plaque has gone. Every time I go back to my hometown, I am heartbroken. Looking back at Yang Gong, I feel lost.

Born Vegetarian 169

— Lan Qian

My friend Liang Jun Kuizhao is a diligent and courageous young man. He studied at Zhijiang University in Hangzhou. The opportunity to return to Shanghai is rare. Last night, I went to Mr. He's house on Sichuan Road. Liang Jun was there. We met unexpectedly. We were very happy. The host was very affectionate and insisted on keeping us for dinner. So we did not leave.

Mr. Liang's nature is very peculiar. He is different from ordinary people. He has not been able to taste meat since he was born. If he smells it, he will vomit. He cannot eat anything other than the first and last two tastes of salty, sour, bitter, spicy, and sweet. He does not eat things with strange tastes. He does not eat chives, onions, or garlic. He only uses green vegetables and tofu to help him eat every day. And the amount of rice he eats is not weak. Therefore, on this evening, the host specially prepared vegetarian dishes to entertain him.

What's more, Mr. Liang does not smoke or drink alcohol. He does not like what is called the nature of food and sex. He said, "I have already studied physiology. I know the structure of the human body, regardless of gender. It's just skin and bones. Why should I pay attention to it?" So Mr. He earnestly said, "There are already more than a hundred kinds of vegetarian food for the mouth and stomach. Frying, stir-frying, stewing, and braising, what taste cannot rival meat? The human body is just a stinky skin bag. Although the food is delicious, what is excreted is the same. Why should we kill more creatures to satisfy our hunger?" (Mr. He is also a strong advocate of vegetarianism). He then turned to Mr. Liang and said, "Your previous life must have been a high monk. But because your merits and virtues are not complete and your sins are not cleansed, the God of Darkness has punished you to come here to experience more vicissitudes. You should encourage yourself."

Not long after the meal, Mr. Liang had to take the night train to Beijing to participate in the grand ceremony of the National Boy Scout General Review. So he left first.

Jui Yu Hsuan's American Travel Notes 170

— Lai

After that, I sent Wan Hua a book on Boston's history. This book was specially bound with a specially made book cover. It was printed with the words "Presented to Mr. Mei". Finally, the most famous members of our community performed to help the rest of the performers. There were two singers, one who played and sang, and one who performed magic. They were all excellent. The guide then showed us the souvenirs in each room. There were many books. Wan presented a painting, a pair of yarn lanterns, and a reply. He said that he was very happy to be welcomed by the people of your country during this trip to the United States. He was especially honored to be promoted and rewarded by the predecessors in the same industry. Lan Fang's artistic skills are still shallow, and I hope that you will give me guidance. Finally, he said that socialists have a saying that workers all over the world should unite. I hope that artists all over the world will unite today. I came here to absorb some new cultures from the New World and contribute to my motherland after I return home. Therefore, I must ask you for more advice. So that this trip is not in vain. I also hope that you will travel to the East together in the future, so that the people of our country can broaden their horizons, and so that Lan Fang can take this opportunity to do his best as a host. That night was extremely enjoyable for both the host and the guests. (March 14)

A few days ago, an old lady watched Wan's play twelve times. It was performed for three weeks and she never saw Wan. She was afraid of bothering Wan. She came to see him yesterday. When I told her that there was still one week left, she said that she wanted to watch it twelve more times but could not. She will come to watch it every day from now on.

There is a Greek newspaper here that is read by literary experts. It is also very popular in Europe. There is a long article that praises Wan Hua very much, but I could not understand it in detail because it is in Greek. I will have someone translate it when I have time.

Recently, the discussions in major venues have mostly been about Wan, and they all say that he is really a great artist and must be seen, etc. For example, Philadelphia has already sent a telegram, and several art conferences are preparing to welcome him.

Dr. Dewey and others invited him to dinner. There were dozens of university professors at the table. Dr. Dewey said that everyone was very happy to see Eastern culture in the United States this time. Mr. Mei's ability to bridge the gap between the two countries can be said to be extremely great.

Consul General Xiong said that Mr. Mei's visit to the United States this time has had an extraordinary impact on Eastern culture and an extraordinary impact on the future relationship between China and the United States. It is a good opportunity to travel to various cities to promote it.

Today's Herald Tribune has an essay that says that Mr. Mei is young and beautiful. This visit to the United States has been very successful. I am also very satisfied with it. The first performance was full, which was expected. However, the seats were still the same after four weeks of performance, which shows the extent to which Americans welcome Chinese opera. Chinese opera has a very high structure and is not easy to learn. However, there is now this opportunity to see this good play and see this complete art. Isn't it a very pleasant thing? It also said that Mr. Mei's performance is not only good, but his personality is also very noble. (March 17)

Food: Rice Market in Hexia Sluggish, Prices Weak 176

▲ Zhabei: Yesterday, the source of inland rice was scarce, and sales in the market were even more sluggish. Although the arrival of rice from Hexia was rare, the existing stock was not weak. Ordinary Northern White Japonica rice had mostly entered the pass at 20 yuan, and the middle and lower grades weakened by a few jiao. Transactions were sparse, and merchants were observing. With the sunny and hot weather, if the accumulated goods in the river are not sold early, they may change color. Therefore, merchants with goods held for a long time intend to sell them quickly, but it is difficult to fulfill their wishes due to the lack of customers. However, the price is gradually declining. Buyers of Bo Dao rice are also rare, and retail sales in this street are limited. Large-scale short-term sales are close to a few jiao. The source of Yang Du Jian rice is still dry, and the outgoing path is also weak. The market is fixed, and Bai Yuan rice is sluggish and continues to weaken, with an unusually sluggish situation.

▲ South Shanghai: The arrival of boats from Hexia is not strong, estimated to be only a few. Sales of Changzhou and Wuxi Northern Japonica rice are flat, and the market is sluggish. The arrival and sales of Su Tong Ji Japonica rice are both stagnant, and the trend is gradually becoming sluggish. The above prices are high and fixed, but the quality is soft, with a difference of about one jiao per batch. The outgoing path of southern Qing Ding and other Bo Dao and early rice is uneven, and sales are very slack. Only a few street merchants are picking and purchasing, and the market is slightly modified. There are some arrivals of foreign pointed rice, but only southern goods, and northern goods are extremely rare. Buying sentiment is average, and large-scale transactions are stable. Currently, the situation of Xian rice has no glory or disgrace to speak of. General sales are still connected, and retail sales are slightly active, with no price fluctuations. Yin Yuan rice is not selling, and transactions are sluggish and sparse, showing a weakening trend of a few jiao.

Silk and Tea: Over 400 Bales of Silk Sold Last Week 177

▲ Chen Silk Gradually Running Out... Prices Increasing

Last week, the silk market of foreign firms and Chinese firms in this city lacked the possibility of continued prosperity. This was because the end of last week coincided with Christmas, and the customs was closed. There were only four market days throughout the week. In addition, exchange rates fluctuated constantly, and overseas silk weaving factories focused on rayon for thin silk, resulting in a reduction in the sales of natural silk. The import of raw silk to New York from China and Japan increased sharply, and the stock of silk was relatively thick. The demand for raw silk in Lyon was increasingly scarce. As Chinese merchants ran out of raw materials and the remaining silk was limited, prices increased. Silk factories will stop reeling in the middle of next month, and silk sales are unlikely to be smooth. Last week, a total of over 400 bales of term and spot silk were traded. The export of Chinese silk was over 2,000 bales, mostly shipped to American territories. Due to exchange rate factors, the price of Chinese silk overseas tended to be flat and weak. The market price of Chinese silk in European and American markets at the end of last week is listed below (New York price per pound, unit: gold yuan; Lyon price per kilo, unit: francs):

Sugar Market: Raw Sugar and White Sugar Slightly Flat 178

▲ Japanese Sugar Market Slightly Declining

Yesterday was Sunday, and there were no telegrams from the production area sugar market. The guild market was flat. Initially, the atmosphere of Dutch sugar No. 24 raw sugar and white sugar was quite strong, and the sellers called for a price of 7 taels and 3 qian and 5 fen. However, there were no buyers, and a certain merchant lowered the price to 7 taels and 3 qian, willing to sell. The market atmosphere suddenly flattened, and buyers became more hesitant, offering even lower prices. After a stalemate, there were slight transactions at 7 taels, 2 qian and 7 and a half fen. Finely ground white sugar was 7 taels and 3 qian and 5 fen, and No. 20 medium sugar white sugar was 7 taels and 5 fen, and the market was still quite strong. Transactions of Japanese sugar were also sparse, and the market slightly declined. N Mark was 7 taels and 7 qian, TY Mark was 7 taels and 6 qian, PY Mark was 7 taels, 7 qian and 7 and a half fen, KT Mark was 7 taels, 6 qian, 1 fen and a half li, and YRO Mark was 7 taels and 3 qian. The market conditions were all flat and weak.

Textiles: Summer Woolen Goods Sales Increase Sharply 179

White Drill, White Zhigong, Sun Cloth, Weiye Chi, Flannel, Benpi Qu, Feather Yarn Cloth, Yellow Twill, Gauze Twill, Tarpaulin, and Shuluo Gauze are all woolen goods that are suitable for the summer market. They have all been launched on the market recently. In recent days, the demand from local merchants has been particularly strong, and sales have been unusually smooth. Among them, Flannel, Benpi Qu, Feather Yarn Cloth, Yellow Twill, White Gauze Twill, and Double Yarn Tarpaulin are the most seasonal goods. The Tongyi Association has opened a lot of orders. It is said that the entire local merchant gang has traded a total of 120 to 130 boxes yesterday. The average overall market price is several fen to one or two qian higher per yard than last year's sales price.

The Leading Lady Problem in Cyrano de Bergerac · Hui · Yin 180

The Fudan Drama Society decided last year to perform the romantic drama Cyrano de Bergerac, which had once caused a sensation in the European and American theater circles. Later, because the director of the society, Mr. Hong Shen, fell ill, this great script was finally unable to be brought to the Chinese stage. This is of course a regret for our comrades who care about the drama movement.

The theater scene in 1930 was considered very active. The Art Drama Society, the Modern Society, etc., were all very hardworking groups. In particular, the drama groups of various schools, since the Modern Society advocated the school drama movement, have become more vigorous in their activities.

The Fudan Drama Society was originally considered to be very prestigious among the universities, and of course it also began to work at this critical juncture. As a result, the sound of preparing for the rehearsal of Cyrano de Bergerac spread throughout the campus again.

Cyrano de Bergerac, as far as we know, requires a lot of actors to play. The male protagonist Cyrano de Bergerac is played by Mr. Hong Shen himself, of course there is no problem. But the female lead Roxane, because of various problems, took a lot of deliberation.

The decision made last semester was to call on Ms. Jin Zhongyu, who had won praise for playing the parasitic grass, to take on the role. But this year, because Ms. Jin is about to graduate and needs to prepare her graduation thesis, she can no longer have a lot of free time to rehearse this heavy Roxane.

I remember there was a message on the school's bulletin board saying that many well-known ladies had been transferred from various places this semester. Of course, Mr. Hong Shen paid close attention to it. So, through the introduction of Ms. Jin, Ms. Yu Jianbi, who had transferred from Zhongda University, was persuaded by Mr. Hong after repeated requests, and agreed to play the role of Roxane.

Ms. Yu is a freshman who just came to Fudan this semester. She originally studied politics at Central University. Later, because Jinling, which had been troubled by a group of wealthy officials and dignitaries, could not keep her fragrant tracks, she resolutely transferred to Fudan, the highest institution of higher learning in the southeast. Anyone who sees Ms. Yu's healthy and beautiful physique, expressive posture, and the naturally melancholy temptation in her speech, will immediately know that it would be best to have her play Roxane in Cyrano de Bergerac.

But, unfortunately, I recently heard that Ms. Yu is not going to play this role anymore. It is said that because Ms. Yu is a freshman, she is very busy with her studies, and she is not very familiar with everything in the school, so she does not want to play this lead role, which feels too burdensome. However, which Miss is Mr. Hong Shen planning to call on to take on this role after all? I heard that he spent a lot of effort when he begged Ms. Yu to take on this role before.

So, Cyrano de Bergerac is prepared to be staged, but the problem of the leading lady has not been decided yet.

The Life of Women Among Overseas Chinese in Nanyang · Y · S 181

I have been wandering in British Malaya since I was a child, so I know a lot about the customs, habits and daily life of Nanyang. Now I will first introduce the life of Chinese women in Nanyang to the Chinese people.

"Status and Occupation" Anyone who has been to Nanyang cannot but believe that Overseas Chinese in Nanyang are full of conservatism. For two or three hundred years, Chinese have lived in the wild land of savage natives, without being assimilated. This is something to be grateful for, but it cannot but be said that it is a gift of their conservatism. Although the trend of the times is evolving day by day, the conservative nature of the Overseas Chinese is still "the same as before." The Chinese women there are still full of the remnants of the old ethics in their minds, and regard the "three obediences and four virtues" of the "Women's Instructions in the Boudoir" as the "golden rule." They can only "marry a pig and follow a pig, marry a dog and follow a dog," and everything must be dependent on the man's thoughts. Therefore, men are happy to support them as toys. They live a comfortable and happy life, and they don't care about status or women's rights.

In recent years, the revolutionary climax in China has gradually affected the Overseas Chinese society in Nanyang. Therefore, the emergence of women's liberation associations and other groups has been heard from time to time. However, in reality, they are still inevitably despised and insulted by men. As for the reason, it is nothing more than the inability to be economically independent. Overseas Chinese women in British Malaya are not prepared in terms of skills and knowledge, so how can their economic status reach the point of independence? In recent years, the singing and dancing stars in China have been welcomed by the local Overseas Chinese after they arrived in Nanyang, and they have become popular for a while. Therefore, all schools have to hire singing and dancing teachers. Therefore, the professional outlet for Overseas Chinese women in Nanyang now is mostly to be singing and dancing teachers, except for a few who are teachers in girls' schools. As for those "Nyonyas" (native women) who have received foreign education, they are only clerks in foreign firms or post and telegraph bureaus. Some poor Overseas Chinese women are mostly hired as servants.

"Clothing" Nanyang is close to the equator, so it is summer all year round. The daily temperature is about 60 to 70 degrees Celsius. Therefore, their clothing is not particular and tends to be simple Malay attire. Moreover, many Overseas Chinese there also marry Malay women as wives, and the resulting natives cannot but be affected by the environment and customs. Ordinary women (referring to native-born Chinese women) mostly wear Malay attire, a red and green apron with rich patterns - Sarong - wrapped around the lower body and extending to the chest, down to the ankles, about four feet long. In addition to the "bodice" on the upper body, they also wear a thin gauze long shirt, the length of which hangs down to the ankles. They wear gold-embroidered slippers barefoot, and the bun is combed on the forehead, with five or six gold or silver hairpins inserted. At first glance, it really makes people suspect that it is ancient Chinese costume. Women dressed like this are called "Nyonyas" by Overseas Chinese. In fact, "Nyonya" is a Malay word, meaning "madam" or "girl", like the English Lady has the same meaning. As for those women who are not natives, they mostly wear the inherent Chinese dress. In recent years, due to the influence of domestic films, these "Nyonyas" have gradually removed their Malay attire and put on Shanghai-style fashions.

"Habits and Language" Because of living with different ethnic groups for a long time, they are inevitably assimilated to some extent. Overseas Chinese women in British Malaya are like people who have been deeply poisoned. They like betel nut, wrapping betel nut and lime "Gambier" in bamboo leaves and sending it into their mouths, chewing carefully, and what they spit out is a liquid that looks like blood. What they exhale is a foul-smelling sour taste. Those who are deeply addicted almost cannot leave their mouths at any time. Therefore, a pair of white teeth will have to become as black and ugly as the teeth of people who smoke opium.

When eating, they mostly use their hands instead of chopsticks, and the utensils for serving rice are mostly plates and dishes, because this way they can feel convenient.

As for the language they speak, it is very complicated, but it is very common to be able to speak at least three languages. Some can even speak five or six languages, such as Malay, English, Hakka, Hokkien, Cantonese, etc. Malay and Hokkien are almost the languages ​​they use daily. Chinese Mandarin, if they have not received Chinese education, can be said to be as rare as phoenix feathers and unicorn horns.

What I have talked about above is just a glimpse of the general situation of the life of Overseas Chinese women in British Malaya. It is inevitable that there will be omissions, but I hope that you readers can pay attention to their lives, whether it is beneficial or harmful to the future of our Overseas Chinese.

Ms. Hobart's Description of China 182

In modern times, people from various European countries have developed an interesting interest in China. Therefore, as long as he writes about the story of China, he can become famous. Especially Western women living in China, they are more likely to have the leisure to write poetry, literature, anecdotes, etc., than capitalist men and women. In the past, Ms. Hack's biography of Du Fu and her works, and Ms. Sisi's volume of Chinese literary research, have all enjoyed great fame in the United States and Britain. Recently, a book by Ms. Alice Tisdale Hobart about the history of a Chinese merchant's romance was published in London, which aroused the interest of Westerners in China. This manuscript is called Pidgin Cargo, which is a description of the romance of a Chinese silk merchant leader. However, many records contain satirical elements. Her husband is an American merchant residing in China, so she spent fifteen years patiently describing it. When the Nanjing Revolution and the fierce battle with Sun Chuanfang broke out two years ago, unfortunately, it caused her fifteen years of hard work to be lost. However, her Chinese servant must have seen the hostess's careful writing over the past fifteen years and knew that it was something of great value, so he desperately rescued the manuscript for her. Now, because of going through such a difficult time, it has aroused people's enthusiastic attention when it was first published in London. (Changxi)
